</p><p>The Renaissance period changed the face of Rome dramatically, with works like the <a href="/wiki/Piet%C3%A0_(Michelangelo)" title="Pietà (Michelangelo)">Pietà</a> by Michelangelo and the frescoes of the <a href="/wiki/Borgia_Apartments" title="Borgia Apartments">Borgia Apartments</a>. Rome reached the highest point of splendour under <a href="/wiki/Pope_Julius_II" title="Pope Julius II">Pope Julius II</a> (1503–1513) and his successors <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_X" title="Pope Leo X">Leo X</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_VII" title="Pope Clement VII">Clement VII</a>, both members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Medici" title="House of Medici">Medici family</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lingelbach_Karneval_in_Rom_001a.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1475" data-file-width="1789" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Lingelbach_Karneval_in_Rom_001a.jpg/220px-Lingelbach_Karneval_in_Rom_001a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Lingelbach_Karneval_in_Rom_001a.jpg/330px-Lingelbach_Karneval_in_Rom_001a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Lingelbach_Karneval_in_Rom_001a.jpg/440px-Lingelbach_Karneval_in_Rom_001a.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lingelbach_Karneval_in_Rom_001a.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Carnival</a> in Rome, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1650</span></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_of_the_Piazza_Navona,_Rome_LACMA_49.17.3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="894" data-file-width="2083" decoding="async" height="94" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/View_of_the_Piazza_Navona%2C_Rome_LACMA_49.17.3.jpg/220px-View_of_the_Piazza_Navona%2C_Rome_LACMA_49.17.3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/View_of_the_Piazza_Navona%2C_Rome_LACMA_49.17.3.jpg/330px-View_of_the_Piazza_Navona%2C_Rome_LACMA_49.17.3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/View_of_the_Piazza_Navona%2C_Rome_LACMA_49.17.3.jpg/440px-View_of_the_Piazza_Navona%2C_Rome_LACMA_49.17.3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:View_of_the_Piazza_Navona,_Rome_LACMA_49.17.3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>A View of the Piazza Navona, Rome</i>, <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Frans_van_Lint" title="Hendrik Frans van Lint">Hendrik Frans van Lint</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1730</span></div></div></div>
<p>In this twenty-year period, Rome became one of the greatest centres of art in the world. The old St. Peter's Basilica built by Emperor <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine the Great</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[65]</a></sup> (which by then was in a dilapidated state) was demolished and a new one begun. The city hosted artists like <a href="/wiki/Ridolfo_Ghirlandaio" title="Ridolfo Ghirlandaio">Ghirlandaio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Perugino" title="Pietro Perugino">Perugino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandro_Botticelli" title="Sandro Botticelli">Botticelli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donato_Bramante" title="Donato Bramante">Bramante</a>, who built the temple of <a href="/wiki/San_Pietro_in_Montorio" title="San Pietro in Montorio">San Pietro in Montorio</a> and planned a great project to renovate the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Palace" title="Apostolic Palace">Vatican</a>. Raphael, who in Rome became one of the most famous painters of Italy, created frescoes in the <a href="/wiki/Villa_Farnesina" title="Villa Farnesina">Villa Farnesina</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Raphael_Rooms" title="Raphael Rooms">Raphael's Rooms</a>, plus many other famous paintings. Michelangelo started the decoration of the ceiling of the Sistine Chapel and executed the famous statue of the <a href="/wiki/Moses" title="Moses">Moses</a> for the tomb of Julius II.
</p><p>Its economy was rich, with the presence of several Tuscan bankers, including <a href="/wiki/Agostino_Chigi" title="Agostino Chigi">Agostino Chigi</a>, who was a friend of Raphael and a patron of arts. Before his early death, Raphael also promoted for the first time the preservation of the ancient ruins. The <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_League_of_Cognac" title="War of the League of Cognac">War of the League of Cognac</a> caused the first plunder of the city in more than five hundred years since <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Rome_(1084)" title="Sack of Rome (1084)">the previous sack</a>; in 1527, the <a href="/wiki/Landsknecht" title="Landsknecht">Landsknechts</a> of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Rome_(1527)" title="Sack of Rome (1527)">sacked the city</a>, bringing an abrupt end to the golden age of the Renaissance in Rome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192522_67-9"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192522-67">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>Beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Trent" title="Council of Trent">Council of Trent</a> in 1545, the Church began the Counter-Reformation in response to the Reformation, a large-scale questioning of the Church's authority on spiritual matters and governmental affairs. This loss of confidence led to major shifts of power away from the Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192522_67-10"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192522-67">[64]</a></sup> Under the popes from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pius_IV" title="Pius IV">Pius IV</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sixtus_V" title="Sixtus V">Sixtus V</a>, Rome became the centre of a reformed Catholicism and saw the building of new monuments which celebrated the papacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192523_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192523-69">[66]</a></sup> The popes and cardinals of the 17th and early 18th centuries continued the movement by having the city's landscape enriched with baroque buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192523_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192523-69">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>This was another nepotistic age; the new aristocratic families (<a href="/wiki/Barberini_family" title="Barberini family">Barberini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pamphili_family" title="Pamphili family">Pamphili</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chigi_family" title="Chigi family">Chigi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rospigliosi_family" title="Rospigliosi family">Rospigliosi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Altieri_family" title="Altieri family">Altieri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Odescalchi_family" title="Odescalchi family">Odescalchi</a>) were protected by their respective popes, who built huge baroque buildings for their relatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192523_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192523-69">[66]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a>, new ideas reached the Eternal City, where the papacy supported archaeological studies and improved the people's welfare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192522_67-11"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192522-67">[64]</a></sup> But not everything went well for the Church during the Counter-Reformation. There were setbacks in the attempts to assert the Church's power, a notable example being in 1773 when Pope Clement XIV was forced by secular powers to have the <a href="/wiki/Suppression_of_the_Society_of_Jesus" title="Suppression of the Society of Jesus">Jesuit order suppressed</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192522_67-12"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBertarelli192522-67">[64]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_modern_and_contemporary">Late modern and contemporary</span></h3>
<p>The rule of the Popes was interrupted by the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic_(18th_century)" title="Roman Republic (18th century)">Roman Republic</a> (1798–1800), which was established under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Papal_States" title="Papal States">Papal States</a> were restored in June 1800, but during <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>'s reign Rome was <a href="/wiki/Rome_(department)" title="Rome (department)">annexed as a <i>Département</i></a> of the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">French Empire</a>: first as <i>Département du Tibre</i> (1808–1810) and then as <i>Département Rome</i> (1810–1814). After the fall of Napoleon, the Papal States were reconstituted by a decision of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> of 1814.
</p><p>In 1849, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Republic_(19th_century)" title="Roman Republic (19th century)">a second Roman Republic</a> was proclaimed during a year of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutions_in_1848" title="Revolutions in 1848">revolutions in 1848</a>. Two of the most influential figures of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">Italian unification</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Mazzini" title="Giuseppe Mazzini">Giuseppe Mazzini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi">Giuseppe Garibaldi</a>, fought for the short-lived republic.
</p><p>Rome then became the focus of hopes of Italian reunification after the rest of Italy was united as the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a> in 1861 with the temporary capital in <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>. That year Rome was declared the capital of Italy even though it was still under the Pope's control. During the 1860s, the last vestiges of the Papal States were under French protection thanks to the foreign policy of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_III" title="Napoleon III">Napoleon III</a>. French troops were stationed in the region under Papal control. In 1870 the French troops were withdrawn due to the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a>. Italian troops were able to <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Rome" title="Capture of Rome">capture Rome</a> entering the city through a breach near <a href="/wiki/Porta_Pia" title="Porta Pia">Porta Pia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IX" title="Pope Pius IX">Pope Pius IX</a> declared himself a <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_in_the_Vatican" title="Prisoner in the Vatican">prisoner in the Vatican</a>. In 1871 the capital of Italy was moved from Florence to Rome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup> In 1870 the population of the city was 212,000, all of whom lived with the area circumscribed by the ancient city, and in 1920, the population was 660,000. A significant portion lived outside the walls in the north and across the Tiber in the Vatican area.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bombardamento_di_Roma.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="524" data-file-width="754" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Bombardamento_di_Roma.gif/220px-Bombardamento_di_Roma.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Bombardamento_di_Roma.gif/330px-Bombardamento_di_Roma.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Bombardamento_di_Roma.gif/440px-Bombardamento_di_Roma.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bombardamento_di_Roma.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bombardment of Rome by <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> planes, 1943</div></div></div>
<p>Soon after World War I in late 1922 Rome witnessed the rise of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Fascism" title="Italian Fascism">Italian Fascism</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>, who led a <a href="/wiki/March_on_Rome" title="March on Rome">march on the city</a>. He did away with democracy by 1926, eventually declaring a new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Italy_(fascist)" title="Imperial Italy (fascist)">Italian Empire</a> and allying Italy with <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> in 1938. Mussolini demolished fairly large parts of the city centre in order to build wide avenues and squares which were supposed to celebrate the fascist regime and the resurgence and glorification of classical Rome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup> The interwar period saw a rapid growth in the city's population which surpassed one million inhabitants soon after 1930. During World War II, due to the art treasuries and the presence of the Vatican, Rome largely escaped the tragic destiny of other European cities. However, on 19 July 1943, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quartiere_San_Lorenzo" title="Quartiere San Lorenzo">San Lorenzo district</a> was <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Rome_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Rome in World War II">subject to Allied bombing raids</a>, resulting in about 3,000 fatalities and 11,000 injuries, of whom another 1,500 died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[69]</a></sup> Mussolini <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Fascist_regime_in_Italy" title="Fall of the Fascist regime in Italy">was arrested on 25 July 1943</a>. On the date of the <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_Cassibile" title="Armistice of Cassibile">Italian Armistice</a> 8 September 1943 the city was occupied by the Germans. The Pope declared Rome an <a href="/wiki/Open_city" title="Open city">open city</a>. It was liberated on 4 June 1944.
</p><p>Rome developed greatly after the war as part of the "<a href="/wiki/Italian_economic_miracle" title="Italian economic miracle">Italian economic miracle</a>" of post-war reconstruction and modernisation in the 1950s and early 1960s. During this period, the years of <i>la dolce vita</i> ("the sweet life"), Rome became a fashionable city, with popular classic films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Ben-Hur_(1959_film)" title="Ben-Hur (1959 film)">Ben Hur</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Quo_Vadis_(1951_film)" title="Quo Vadis (1951 film)">Quo Vadis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Roman_Holiday" title="Roman Holiday">Roman Holiday</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/La_Dolce_Vita" title="La Dolce Vita">La Dolce Vita</a></i> filmed in the city's iconic <a href="/wiki/Cinecitt%C3%A0" title="Cinecittà">Cinecittà Studios</a>. The rising trend in population growth continued until the mid-1980s when the <i>comune</i> had more than 2.8 million residents. After this, the population declined slowly as people began to move to nearby suburbs.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Rome" title="Mayor of Rome">Mayor of Rome</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_Council_of_Rome" title="City Council of Rome">City Council of Rome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Rome" title="Elections in Rome">Elections in Rome</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Administrative_subdivisions_of_Rome" title="Administrative subdivisions of Rome">Administrative subdivisions of Rome</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span></h3>
<p>Rome constitutes a comune <i><a href="/wiki/Comune" title="Comune">speciale</a></i>, named <i>"Roma Capitale"</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup> and is the largest both in terms of land area and population among the 8,101 <i>comuni</i> of Italy. It is governed by a mayor and a city council. The seat of the <i>comune</i> is the <i>Palazzo Senatorio</i> on the <a href="/wiki/Capitoline_Hill" title="Capitoline Hill">Capitoline Hill</a>, the historic seat of the city government. The local administration in Rome is commonly referred to as <i>"Campidoglio"</i>, the Italian name of the hill.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_and_historical_subdivisions">Administrative and historical subdivisions</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roma_-_Municipi_numerata.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="618" data-file-width="796" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Roma_-_Municipi_numerata.png/220px-Roma_-_Municipi_numerata.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Roma_-_Municipi_numerata.png/330px-Roma_-_Municipi_numerata.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Roma_-_Municipi_numerata.png/440px-Roma_-_Municipi_numerata.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roma_-_Municipi_numerata.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i>municipi</i> of Rome</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Piazza_de_la_Republica_-_Roma_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Piazza_de_la_Republica_-_Roma_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Piazza_de_la_Republica_-_Roma_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Piazza_de_la_Republica_-_Roma_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Piazza_de_la_Republica_-_Roma_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Piazza_de_la_Republica_-_Roma_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Piazza_de_la_Republica_-_Roma_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Piazza_de_la_Republica_-_Roma_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Piazza_della_Repubblica,_Rome" title="Piazza della Repubblica, Rome">Piazza della Repubblica, Rome</a></div></div></div>
<p>Since 1972, the city has been divided into administrative areas, called <i>municipi</i> (sing. <i>municipio</i>) (until 2001 named <i>circoscrizioni</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[71]</a></sup> They were created for administrative reasons to increase decentralisation in the city. Each <i>municipio</i> is governed by a president and a council of twenty-five members who are elected by its residents every five years. The <i>municipi</i> frequently cross the boundaries of the traditional, non-administrative divisions of the city. The municipi were originally 20, then 19,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup> and in 2013, their number was reduced to 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rome is also divided into differing types of non-administrative units. The historic centre is divided into 22 <i><a href="/wiki/Rioni_of_Rome" title="Rioni of Rome">rioni</a></i>, all of which are located within the <a href="/wiki/Aurelian_Walls" title="Aurelian Walls">Aurelian Walls</a> except <a href="/wiki/Prati" title="Prati">Prati</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borgo_(rione_of_Rome)" title="Borgo (rione of Rome)">Borgo</a>. These originate from the <a href="/wiki/14_regions_of_Augustan_Rome" title="14 regions of Augustan Rome">14 regions of Augustan Rome</a>, which evolved in the Middle Ages into the <a href="/wiki/14_regions_of_Medieval_Rome" title="14 regions of Medieval Rome">medieval rioni</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, under Pope <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sixtus_V" title="Sixtus V">Sixtus V</a>, they again reached fourteen, and their boundaries were finally defined under <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XIV" title="Pope Benedict XIV">Pope Benedict XIV</a> in 1743.
</p><p>A new subdivision of the city under <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> was ephemeral, and there were no serious changes in the organisation of the city until 1870 when Rome became the third capital of Italy. The needs of the new capital led to an explosion both in the urbanisation and in the population within and outside the <a href="/wiki/Aurelian_Walls" title="Aurelian Walls">Aurelian walls</a>. In 1874, a fifteenth rione, <a href="/wiki/Esquilino_(rione_of_Rome)" title="Esquilino (rione of Rome)">Esquilino</a>, was created on the newly urbanised zone of <a href="/wiki/Monti_(rione_of_Rome)" title="Monti (rione of Rome)">Monti</a>. At the beginning of the 20th century other rioni were created (the last one was Prati – the only one outside the Walls of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Urban_VIII" title="Pope Urban VIII">Pope Urban VIII</a> – in 1921). Afterwards, for the new administrative subdivisions of the city, the term "quartiere" was used. Today all the rioni are part of the first Municipio, which therefore coincides completely with the <i>historical city</i> (<i>Centro Storico</i>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_and_regional_government">Metropolitan and regional government</span></h3>
<p>Rome is the principal town of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_City_of_Rome" title="Metropolitan City of Rome">Metropolitan City of Rome</a>, operative since 1 January 2015. The Metropolitan City replaced the old <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Rome" title="Province of Rome">provincia di Roma</a>, which included the city's metropolitan area and extends further north until <a href="/wiki/Civitavecchia" title="Civitavecchia">Civitavecchia</a>. The Metropolitan City of Rome is the largest by area in Italy. At 5,352 km<sup>2</sup> (2,066 sq mi), its dimensions are comparable to the region of <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">Liguria</a>. Moreover, the city is also the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Lazio" title="Lazio">Lazio</a> region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_government">National government</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quirinale_palazzo_e_obelisco_con_dioscuri_Roma.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4912" data-file-width="6965" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Quirinale_palazzo_e_obelisco_con_dioscuri_Roma.jpg/220px-Quirinale_palazzo_e_obelisco_con_dioscuri_Roma.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Quirinale_palazzo_e_obelisco_con_dioscuri_Roma.jpg/330px-Quirinale_palazzo_e_obelisco_con_dioscuri_Roma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Quirinale_palazzo_e_obelisco_con_dioscuri_Roma.jpg/440px-Quirinale_palazzo_e_obelisco_con_dioscuri_Roma.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quirinale_palazzo_e_obelisco_con_dioscuri_Roma.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palazzo_del_Quirinale" title="Palazzo del Quirinale">Palazzo del Quirinale</a>, now seat of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Italy" title="President of Italy">President of the Italian Republic</a></div></div></div>
<p>Rome is the national capital of Italy and is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Italy" title="Politics of Italy">Italian Government</a>. The official residences of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Italy" title="President of Italy">President of the Italian Republic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Italy" title="Prime Minister of Italy">Italian Prime Minister</a>, the seats of both houses of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Italy" title="Parliament of Italy">Italian Parliament</a> and that of the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Italy" title="Constitutional Court of Italy">Italian Constitutional Court</a> are located in the historic centre. The state ministries are spread out around the city; these include the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which is located in <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_della_Farnesina" title="Palazzo della Farnesina">Palazzo della Farnesina</a> near the Olympic stadium.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span></h3>
<p>Rome is in the <a href="/wiki/Lazio" title="Lazio">Lazio</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Central_Italy" title="Central Italy">central Italy</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Tiber" title="Tiber">Tiber</a> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">Tevere</i>) river. The original settlement developed on hills that faced onto a ford beside the <a href="/wiki/Tiber_Island" title="Tiber Island">Tiber Island</a>, the only natural ford of the river in this area. The Rome of the Kings was built on seven hills: the <a href="/wiki/Aventine_Hill" title="Aventine Hill">Aventine Hill</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caelian_Hill" title="Caelian Hill">Caelian Hill</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capitoline_Hill" title="Capitoline Hill">Capitoline Hill</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Esquiline_Hill" title="Esquiline Hill">Esquiline Hill</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Palatine_Hill" title="Palatine Hill">Palatine Hill</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Quirinal_Hill" title="Quirinal Hill">Quirinal Hill</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Viminal_Hill" title="Viminal Hill">Viminal Hill</a>. Modern Rome is also crossed by another river, the <a href="/wiki/Aniene" title="Aniene">Aniene</a>, which flows into the Tiber north of the historic centre.
</p><p>Although the city centre is about 24 km (15 mi) inland from the <a href="/wiki/Tyrrhenian_Sea" title="Tyrrhenian Sea">Tyrrhenian Sea</a>, the city territory extends to the shore, where the south-western district of <a href="/wiki/Ostia_(Rome)" title="Ostia (Rome)">Ostia</a> is located. The altitude of the central part of Rome ranges from 13 m (43 ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> (at the base of the <a href="/wiki/Pantheon,_Rome" title="Pantheon, Rome">Pantheon</a>) to 139 m (456 ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> (the peak of <a href="/wiki/Monte_Mario" title="Monte Mario">Monte Mario</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup> The <i>Comune</i> of Rome covers an overall area of about 1,285 km<sup>2</sup> (496 sq mi), including many green areas.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rome_by_Sentinel-2,_2020-12-21.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8894" data-file-width="8049" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Rome_by_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-12-21.jpg/220px-Rome_by_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-12-21.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Rome_by_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-12-21.jpg/330px-Rome_by_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-12-21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Rome_by_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-12-21.jpg/440px-Rome_by_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-12-21.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rome_by_Sentinel-2,_2020-12-21.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite image of Rome</div></div></div>
<p>Throughout the history of Rome, the urban limits of the city were considered to be the area within the city's walls. Originally, these consisted of the <a href="/wiki/Servian_Wall" title="Servian Wall">Servian Wall</a>, which was built twelve years after the <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaulish</a> sack of the city in 390 BC. This contained most of the Esquiline and Caelian hills, as well as the whole of the other five. Rome outgrew the Servian Wall, but no more walls were constructed until almost 700 years later, when, in 270 AD, Emperor <a href="/wiki/Aurelian" title="Aurelian">Aurelian</a> began building the <a href="/wiki/Aurelian_Walls" title="Aurelian Walls">Aurelian Walls</a>. These were almost 19 km (12 mi) long, and were still the walls the troops of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a> had to breach to enter the city in 1870. The city's urban area is cut in two by its ring-road, the <i><a href="/wiki/Grande_Raccordo_Anulare" title="Grande Raccordo Anulare">Grande Raccordo Anulare</a></i> ("GRA"), finished in 1962, which circles the city centre at a distance of about 10 km (6 mi). Although when the ring was completed most parts of the inhabited area lay inside it (one of the few exceptions was the former village of <a href="/wiki/Ostia_(Rome)" title="Ostia (Rome)">Ostia</a>, which lies along the Tyrrhenian coast), in the meantime quarters have been built which extend up to 20 km (12 mi) beyond it.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The <i>comune</i> covers an area roughly three times the total area within the <i>Raccordo</i> and is comparable in area to the entire metropolitan cities of <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>, and to an area six times the size of the territory of these cities. It also includes considerable areas of abandoned marshland which is suitable neither for agriculture nor for urban development.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>As a consequence, the density of the <i>comune</i> is not that high, its territory being divided between highly urbanised areas and areas designated as parks, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nature_reserves" title="Nature reserves">nature reserves</a>, and for agricultural use.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Rome" title="Climate of Rome">Climate of Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Doria_Pamphili_6376.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Doria_Pamphili_6376.jpg/220px-Doria_Pamphili_6376.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Doria_Pamphili_6376.jpg/330px-Doria_Pamphili_6376.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Doria_Pamphili_6376.jpg/440px-Doria_Pamphili_6376.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Doria_Pamphili_6376.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stone pines in the <a href="/wiki/Villa_Doria_Pamphili" title="Villa Doria Pamphili">Villa Doria Pamphili</a></div></div></div>
<p>Rome has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot-summer_Mediterranean_climate" title="Hot-summer Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <i>Csa</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[77]</a></sup> with hot, dry summers and mild, humid winters.
</p><p>Its average annual temperature is above 21 °C (70 °F) during the day and 9 °C (48 °F) at night. In the coldest month, January, the average temperature is 12.6 °C (54.7 °F) during the day and 2.1 °C (35.8 °F) at night. In the warmest month, August, the average temperature is 31.7 °C (89.1 °F) during the day and 17.3 °C (63.1 °F) at night.
</p><p>December, January and February are the coldest months, with a daily mean temperature of approximately 8 °C (46 °F). Temperatures during these months generally vary between 10 and 15 °C (50 and 59 °F) during the day and between 3 and 5 °C (37 and 41 °F) at night, with colder or warmer spells occurring frequently. Snowfall is rare but not unheard of, with light snow or flurries occurring on some winters, generally without accumulation, and major snowfalls on a very rare occurrence (the most recent ones were in 2018, 2012 and 1986).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>The average <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relative_humidity" title="Relative humidity">relative humidity</a> is 75%, varying from 72% in July to 77% in November. Sea temperatures vary from a low of 13.9 °C (57.0 °F) in February to a high of 25.0 °C (77.0 °F) in August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seatemperature.org2_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-seatemperature.org2-84">[81]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Italy" title="Demographics of Italy">Demographics of Italy</a></div>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-top-width:0;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><caption style="border-top:1px #aaa solid;border-left:1px #aaa solid;border-right:1px #aaa solid;background-color:lavender;padding:0.25em;font-weight:bold">Historical population</caption><tbody><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Population">Pop.</abbr></th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Percent change">±%</abbr></th></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1861 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">194,500</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">—    </td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1871 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">212,432</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+9.2%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1881 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">273,952</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">660,235</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+27.2%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1931 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">1,150,589</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+23.6%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1951 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">1,651,754</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+43.6%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">1961 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">2,188,160</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+32.5%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1991 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,775,250</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">−2.3%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2001 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,663,182</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">−4.0%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">2011 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">2,617,175</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">−1.7%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2017 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,876,051</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+9.9%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Statistics_(Italy)" title="National Institute of Statistics (Italy)">ISTAT</a>, 2001</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In 550 BC, Rome was the second largest city in Italy, with <a href="/wiki/Taranto" title="Taranto">Tarentum</a> being the largest.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It had an area of about 285 ha (700 acres) and an estimated population of 35,000. Other sources suggest the population was just under 100,000 from 600 to 500 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup> When the Republic was founded in 509 BC the census recorded a population of 130,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[85]</a></sup> The republic included the city itself and the immediate surroundings. Other sources suggest a population of 150,000 in 500 BC. It surpassed 300,000 in 150 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[90]</a></sup>
</p><p>The size of the city at the time of the Emperor <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> is a matter of speculation, with estimates based on grain distribution, grain imports, aqueduct capacity, city limits, population density, census reports, and assumptions about the number of unreported women, children and slaves providing a very wide range. Glenn Storey estimates 450,000 people, Whitney Oates estimates 1.2 million, Neville Morely provides a rough estimate of 800,000 and excludes earlier suggestions of 2 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> Estimates of the city's population towards and after the end of the Roman empire also vary. A.H.M. Jones estimated the population at 650,000 in the mid-fifth century. The damage caused by the sackings may have been overestimated. The population had already started to decline from the late fourth century onward, although around the middle of the fifth century it seems that Rome continued to be the most populous city of the two parts of the Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup> According to Krautheimer it was still close to 800,000 in 400 AD; had declined to 500,000 by 452, and dwindled to perhaps 100,000 in 500 AD. After the Gothic Wars, 535–552, the population may have dwindled temporarily to 30,000. During the pontificate of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Gregory_I" title="Pope Gregory I">Pope Gregory I</a> (590–604), it may have reached 90,000, augmented by refugees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup> Lancon estimates 500,000 based on the number of 'incisi' enrolled as eligible to receive bread, oil and wine rations; the number fell to 120,000 in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Reform_of_419&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Reform of 419 (page does not exist)">reform of 419</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup> Neil Christie, citing free rations for the poorest, estimated 500,000 in the mid-fifth century and still a quarter of a million at the end of the century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup> Novel 36 of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Valentinian_III" title="Valentinian III">Valentinian III</a> records 3.629 million pounds of pork to be distributed to the needy at 5 lbs. per month for the five winter months, sufficient for 145,000 recipients. This has been used to suggest a population of just under 500,000. Supplies of grain remained steady until the seizure of the remaining provinces of North Africa in 439 by the <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>, and may have continued to some degree afterwards for a while. The city's population declined to less than 50,000 people in the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">Early Middle Ages</a> from 700 AD onward. It continued to stagnate or shrink until the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p>When the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a> annexed Rome in 1870, the city had a population of about 225,000. Less than half the city within the walls was built up in 1881 when the population recorded was 275,000. This increased to 600,000 by the eve of World War I. The <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">Fascist</a> regime of Mussolini tried to block an excessive demographic rise of the city but failed to prevent it from reaching one million people by the early 1930s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Population growth continued after the Second World War, helped by a post-war economic boom. A construction boom also created many suburbs during the 1950s and 1960s.
</p><p>In mid-2010, there were 2,754,440 residents in the city proper, while some 4.2 million people lived in the greater Rome area (which can be approximately identified with its administrative metropolitan city, with a population density of about 800 inhabitants/km<sup>2</sup> stretching over more than 5,000 km<sup>2</sup> (1,900 sq mi)). Minors (children ages 18 and younger) totalled 17.00% of the population compared to pensioners who number 20.76%. This compares with the Italian average of 18.06% (minors) and 19.94% (pensioners). The average age of a Roman resident is 43 compared to the Italian average of 42. In the five years between 2002 and 2007, the population of Rome grew by 6.54%, while Italy as a whole grew by 3.56%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup> The current<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> birth rate of Rome is 9.10 births per 1,000 inhabitants compared to the Italian average of 9.45 births.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The urban area of Rome extends beyond the administrative city limits with a population of around 3.9 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Urban_Areas_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_Urban_Areas-104">[101]</a></sup> Between 3.2 and 4.2 million people live in the <a href="/wiki/Rome_metropolitan_area" title="Rome metropolitan area">Rome metropolitan area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[106]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Esquilino_da_s_M_Maggiore_1240961.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Esquilino_da_s_M_Maggiore_1240961.JPG/220px-Esquilino_da_s_M_Maggiore_1240961.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Esquilino_da_s_M_Maggiore_1240961.JPG/330px-Esquilino_da_s_M_Maggiore_1240961.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Esquilino_da_s_M_Maggiore_1240961.JPG/440px-Esquilino_da_s_M_Maggiore_1240961.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Esquilino_da_s_M_Maggiore_1240961.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Esquilino_(rione_of_Rome)" title="Esquilino (rione of Rome)">Esquilino</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Rioni_of_Rome" title="Rioni of Rome">rione</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>According to the latest statistics conducted by ISTAT,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[107]</a></sup> approximately 9.5% of the population consists of non-Italians. About half of the immigrant population consists of those of various other European origins (chiefly Romanian, Polish, Ukrainian, and Albanian) numbering a combined total of 131,118 or 4.7% of the population. The remaining 4.8% are those with non-European origins, chiefly <a href="/wiki/Filipinos" title="Filipinos">Filipinos</a> (26,933), Bangladeshis (12,154), and Chinese (10,283).
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Esquilino_(rione_of_Rome)" title="Esquilino (rione of Rome)">Esquilino</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Rioni_of_Rome" title="Rioni of Rome">rione</a></i>, off <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Termini_Station_(Rome)" title="Termini Station (Rome)">Termini Railway Station</a>, has evolved into a largely immigrant neighbourhood. It is perceived as Rome's Chinatown. Immigrants from more than a hundred different countries reside there. A commercial district, Esquilino contains restaurants featuring many kinds of international cuisine. There are wholesale clothes shops. Of the 1,300 or so commercial premises operating in the district 800 are Chinese-owned; around 300 are run by immigrants from other countries around the world; 200 are owned by Italians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[108]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Rome" title="List of people from Rome">List of people from Rome</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Rome" title="Religion in Rome">Religion in Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Giovanni_in_Laterano_-_Rome.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2649" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/San_Giovanni_in_Laterano_-_Rome.jpg/220px-San_Giovanni_in_Laterano_-_Rome.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/San_Giovanni_in_Laterano_-_Rome.jpg/330px-San_Giovanni_in_Laterano_-_Rome.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/San_Giovanni_in_Laterano_-_Rome.jpg/440px-San_Giovanni_in_Laterano_-_Rome.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Giovanni_in_Laterano_-_Rome.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Archbasilica_of_Saint_John_Lateran" title="Archbasilica of Saint John Lateran">Archbasilica of Saint John Lateran</a>, Rome's Cathedral, built in 324, and partly rebuilt between 1660 and 1734</div></div></div>
<p>Much like the rest of Italy, Rome is predominantly <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a>, and the city has been an important centre of religion and <a href="/wiki/Christian_pilgrimage" title="Christian pilgrimage">pilgrimage</a> for centuries, the base of the ancient Roman religion with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontifex_Maximus" title="Pontifex Maximus">pontifex maximus</a> and later the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Vatican</a> and the pope. Before the arrival of the Christians in Rome, the <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_ancient_Rome" title="Religion in ancient Rome">Religio Romana</a> (literally, the "Roman Religion") was the major religion of the city in classical antiquity. The first gods held sacred by the Romans were <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_(mythology)" title="Jupiter (mythology)">Jupiter</a>, the Most High, and <a href="/wiki/Mars_(mythology)" title="Mars (mythology)">Mars</a>, the god of war, and father of Rome's twin founders, <a href="/wiki/Romulus_and_Remus" title="Romulus and Remus">Romulus and Remus</a>, according to tradition. Other deities such as <a href="/wiki/Vesta_(mythology)" title="Vesta (mythology)">Vesta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minerva" title="Minerva">Minerva</a> were honoured. Rome was also the base of several mystery cults, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mithraic_Mysteries" title="Mithraic Mysteries">Mithraism</a>. Later, after <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">St Peter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">St Paul</a> were martyred in the city, and the first Christians began to arrive, Rome became Christian, and the <a href="/wiki/Old_St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="Old St. Peter's Basilica">Old St. Peter's Basilica</a> was constructed in 313 AD. Despite some interruptions (such as the <a href="/wiki/Avignon_Papacy" title="Avignon Papacy">Avignon papacy</a>), Rome has for centuries been the home of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Bishop of Rome</a>, otherwise known as the Pope.
</p><p>Despite the fact that Rome is home to the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> and St. Peter's Basilica, Rome's cathedral is the <a href="/wiki/Archbasilica_of_Saint_John_Lateran" title="Archbasilica of Saint John Lateran">Archbasilica of Saint John Lateran</a>, in the south-east of the city centre. There are around 900 churches in Rome in total. Aside from the cathedral itself, some others of note include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basilica_di_Santa_Maria_Maggiore" title="Basilica di Santa Maria Maggiore">Basilica di Santa Maria Maggiore</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Saint_Paul_Outside_the_Walls" title="Basilica of Saint Paul Outside the Walls">Basilica of Saint Paul Outside the Walls</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basilica_di_San_Clemente" title="Basilica di San Clemente">Basilica di San Clemente</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Carlo_alle_Quattro_Fontane" title="San Carlo alle Quattro Fontane">San Carlo alle Quattro Fontane</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Gesu" title="Church of the Gesu">Church of the Gesù</a>. There are also the ancient <a href="/wiki/Catacombs_of_Rome" title="Catacombs of Rome">Catacombs of Rome</a> underneath the city. Numerous highly important religious educational institutions are also in Rome, such as the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Lateran_University" title="Pontifical Lateran University">Pontifical Lateran University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Biblical_Institute" title="Pontifical Biblical Institute">Pontifical Biblical Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Gregorian_University" title="Pontifical Gregorian University">Pontifical Gregorian University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Oriental_Institute" title="Pontifical Oriental Institute">Pontifical Oriental Institute</a>.
</p><p>Since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a>, Rome is also the centre of an important <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> community,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[109]</a></sup> which was once based in <a href="/wiki/Trastevere" title="Trastevere">Trastevere</a>, and later in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Ghetto" title="Roman Ghetto">Roman Ghetto</a>. There lies also the major synagogue in Rome, the <i><a href="/wiki/Great_Synagogue_of_Rome" title="Great Synagogue of Rome">Tempio Maggiore</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vatican_City">Vatican City</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1008px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vatikan_Kolonaden_Petersdom.jpg" title="St. Peter's Square in Vatican City"><img alt="Panorama of St. Peter's Square" data-file-height="1353" data-file-width="7500" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Vatikan_Kolonaden_Petersdom.jpg/1000px-Vatikan_Kolonaden_Petersdom.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Vatikan_Kolonaden_Petersdom.jpg/1500px-Vatikan_Kolonaden_Petersdom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Vatikan_Kolonaden_Petersdom.jpg/2000px-Vatikan_Kolonaden_Petersdom.jpg 2x" width="1000"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vatikan_Kolonaden_Petersdom.jpg" title="File:Vatikan Kolonaden Petersdom.jpg"> </a></div><a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Square" title="St. Peter's Square">St. Peter's Square</a> in Vatican City</div></div></div>
<p>The territory of <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> is part of the <i>Mons Vaticanus</i> (<a href="/wiki/Vatican_Hill" title="Vatican Hill">Vatican Hill</a>), and of the adjacent former Vatican Fields, where <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">St. Peter's Basilica</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Palace" title="Apostolic Palace">Apostolic Palace</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel" title="Sistine Chapel">Sistine Chapel</a>, and museums were built, along with various other buildings. The area was part of the Roman <a href="/wiki/Rione" title="Rione">rione</a> of <a href="/wiki/Borgo_(rione_of_Rome)" title="Borgo (rione of Rome)">Borgo</a> until 1929. Being separated from the city on the west bank of the <a href="/wiki/Tiber" title="Tiber">Tiber</a>, the area was a suburb that was protected by being included within the walls of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_IV" title="Pope Leo IV">Leo IV</a>, later expanded by the current fortification walls of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_III" title="Pope Paul III">Paul III</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IV" title="Pope Pius IV">Pius IV</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Urban_VIII" title="Pope Urban VIII">Urban VIII</a>.
</p><p>When the <a href="/wiki/Lateran_Treaty" title="Lateran Treaty">Lateran Treaty</a> of 1929 that created the Vatican state was being prepared, the boundaries of the proposed territory were influenced by the fact that much of it was all but enclosed by this loop. For some parts of the border, there was no wall, but the line of certain buildings supplied part of the boundary, and for a small part a new wall was constructed.
</p><p>The territory includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Peter%27s_Square" title="Saint Peter's Square">Saint Peter's Square</a>, separated from the territory of Italy only by a white line along with the limit of the square, where it borders Piazza Pio XII. St. Peter's Square is reached through the <a href="/wiki/Via_della_Conciliazione" title="Via della Conciliazione">Via della Conciliazione</a>, which runs from the Tiber to St. Peter's. This grand approach was designed by architects <a href="/wiki/Marcello_Piacentini" title="Marcello Piacentini">Piacentini</a> and Spaccarelli, on the instructions of <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a> and in accordance with the church, after the conclusion of the <a href="/wiki/Lateran_Treaty" title="Lateran Treaty">Lateran Treaty</a>. According to the Treaty, certain <a href="/wiki/Properties_of_the_Holy_See" title="Properties of the Holy See">properties of the Holy See</a> located in Italian territory, most notably the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papal_Palace_of_Castel_Gandolfo" title="Papal Palace of Castel Gandolfo">Papal Palace of Castel Gandolfo</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_basilica" title="Major basilica">major basilicas</a>, enjoy extraterritorial status similar to that of foreign <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_mission" title="Diplomatic mission">embassies</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pilgrimage">Pilgrimage</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Petersdom_bei_Nacht_Via_della_Conciliazione_in_Rome.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Petersdom_bei_Nacht_Via_della_Conciliazione_in_Rome.jpg/220px-Petersdom_bei_Nacht_Via_della_Conciliazione_in_Rome.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Petersdom_bei_Nacht_Via_della_Conciliazione_in_Rome.jpg/330px-Petersdom_bei_Nacht_Via_della_Conciliazione_in_Rome.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Petersdom_bei_Nacht_Via_della_Conciliazione_in_Rome.jpg/440px-Petersdom_bei_Nacht_Via_della_Conciliazione_in_Rome.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Petersdom_bei_Nacht_Via_della_Conciliazione_in_Rome.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St. Peter's Basilica at night from <a href="/wiki/Via_della_Conciliazione" title="Via della Conciliazione">Via della Conciliazione</a> in Rome</div></div></div>
<p>Rome has been a major <a href="/wiki/Christian_pilgrimage" title="Christian pilgrimage">Christian pilgrimage</a> site since the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. People from all over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_world" title="Christian world">Christian world</a> visit Vatican City, within the city of Rome, the seat of the papacy. The city became a major <a href="/wiki/Pilgrimage" title="Pilgrimage">pilgrimage</a> site during the Middle Ages. Apart from brief periods as an independent city during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, Rome kept its status as Papal capital and holy city for centuries, even when the Papacy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avignon_papacy" title="Avignon papacy">briefly relocated</a> to <a href="/wiki/Avignon" title="Avignon">Avignon</a> (1309–1377). Catholics believe that the Vatican is the last resting place of St. Peter.
</p><p>Pilgrimages to Rome can involve visits to many sites, both within Vatican City and in Italian territory. A popular stopping point is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scala_sancta" title="Scala sancta">Pilate's stairs</a>: these are, according to the Christian tradition, the steps that led up to the <a href="/wiki/Praetorium" title="Praetorium">praetorium</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pontius_Pilate" title="Pontius Pilate">Pontius Pilate</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>, which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" title="Jesus Christ">Jesus Christ</a> stood on during his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Passion_(Christianity)" title="Passion (Christianity)">Passion</a> on his way to trial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[110]</a></sup> The stairs were, reputedly, brought to Rome by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Helena_of_Constantinople" title="Helena of Constantinople">Helena of Constantinople</a> in the fourth century. For centuries, the <i>Scala Santa</i> has attracted Christian pilgrims who wished to honour the Passion of Jesus. Other objects of pilgrimage include several catacombs built in imperial times, in which Christians prayed, buried their dead and performed worship during periods of persecution, and various national churches (among them <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Luigi_dei_francesi" title="San Luigi dei francesi">San Luigi dei francesi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_dell%27Anima" title="Santa Maria dell'Anima">Santa Maria dell'Anima</a>), or churches associated with individual religious orders, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">Jesuit</a> Churches of Jesus and Sant'Ignazio.
</p><p>Traditionally, pilgrims in Rome (as well as devout Romans) visit the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Pilgrim_Churches_of_Rome" title="Seven Pilgrim Churches of Rome">seven pilgrim churches</a> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">Le sette chiese</i>) in 24 hours. This custom, mandatory for each pilgrim in the Middle Ages, was codified in the 16th century by Saint <a href="/wiki/Philip_Neri" title="Philip Neri">Philip Neri</a>. The seven churches are the four major basilicas (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basilica_of_St_Peter" title="Basilica of St Peter">St Peter in the Vatican</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Paul_outside_the_Walls" title="St Paul outside the Walls">St Paul outside the Walls</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_John_in_Lateran" title="St John in Lateran">St John in Lateran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_Maggiore" title="Santa Maria Maggiore">Santa Maria Maggiore</a>), while the other three are <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo_fuori_le_mura" title="San Lorenzo fuori le mura">San Lorenzo fuori le mura</a> (an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Christian" title="Early Christian">Early Christian</a> basilica), <a href="/wiki/Santa_Croce_in_Gerusalemme" title="Santa Croce in Gerusalemme">Santa Croce in Gerusalemme</a> (a church founded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Helena_(empress)" title="Helena (empress)">Helena</a>, the mother of Constantine, which hosts fragments of wood attributed to the holy cross) and <a href="/wiki/San_Sebastiano_fuori_le_mura" title="San Sebastiano fuori le mura">San Sebastiano fuori le mura</a> (which lies on the <a href="/wiki/Appian_Way" title="Appian Way">Appian Way</a> and is built above the <a href="/wiki/Catacombs_of_San_Sebastiano" title="Catacombs of San Sebastiano">Catacombs of San Sebastiano</a>).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_tourist_attractions_in_Rome" title="List of tourist attractions in Rome">List of tourist attractions in Rome</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_streets_in_Rome" title="List of streets in Rome">List of streets in Rome</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Rome" title="Architecture of Rome">Architecture of Rome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Churches_of_Rome" title="Churches of Rome">Churches of Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20190406-DSC5193_Panteon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/20190406-DSC5193_Panteon.jpg/220px-20190406-DSC5193_Panteon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/20190406-DSC5193_Panteon.jpg/330px-20190406-DSC5193_Panteon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/20190406-DSC5193_Panteon.jpg/440px-20190406-DSC5193_Panteon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20190406-DSC5193_Panteon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Pantheon,_Rome" title="Pantheon, Rome">Pantheon</a>, built as a temple dedicated to "all the gods of the past, present and future"</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rome_(IT),_Kolosseum_--_2013_--_3400.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3138" data-file-width="4707" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Rome_%28IT%29%2C_Kolosseum_--_2013_--_3400.jpg/220px-Rome_%28IT%29%2C_Kolosseum_--_2013_--_3400.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Rome_%28IT%29%2C_Kolosseum_--_2013_--_3400.jpg/330px-Rome_%28IT%29%2C_Kolosseum_--_2013_--_3400.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Rome_%28IT%29%2C_Kolosseum_--_2013_--_3400.jpg/440px-Rome_%28IT%29%2C_Kolosseum_--_2013_--_3400.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rome_(IT),_Kolosseum_--_2013_--_3400.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Colosseum" title="Colosseum">Colosseum</a> is still today the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amphitheater" title="Amphitheater">amphitheater</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[111]</a></sup> It was used for <a href="/wiki/Gladiator" title="Gladiator">gladiator</a> shows and other public events (hunting shows, recreations of famous battles and dramas based on classical mythology).</div></div></div>
<p>Rome's architecture over the centuries has greatly developed, especially from the Classical and Imperial Roman styles to modern <a href="/wiki/Fascist_architecture" title="Fascist architecture">fascist architecture</a>. Rome was for a period one of the world's main epicentres of <a href="/wiki/Classical_architecture" title="Classical architecture">classical architecture</a>, developing new forms such as the <a href="/wiki/Arch" title="Arch">arch</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dome" title="Dome">dome</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vault_(architecture)" title="Vault (architecture)">vault</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eyewitness_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eyewitness-115">[112]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> style in the 11th, 12th, and 13th centuries was also widely used in Roman architecture, and later the city became one of the main centres of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neoclassical architecture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eyewitness_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-Eyewitness-115">[112]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_Rome">Ancient Rome</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_ancient_monuments_in_Rome" title="List of ancient monuments in Rome">List of ancient monuments in Rome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Roman_architecture" title="Ancient Roman architecture">Ancient Roman architecture</a></div>
<p>One of the symbols of Rome is the <a href="/wiki/Colosseum" title="Colosseum">Colosseum</a> (70–80 AD), the largest <a href="/wiki/Amphitheatre" title="Amphitheatre">amphitheatre</a> ever built in the Roman Empire. Originally capable of seating 60,000 spectators, it was used for <a href="/wiki/Gladiator" title="Gladiator">gladiatorial</a> combat. Important monuments and sites of ancient Rome include the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Forum" title="Roman Forum">Roman Forum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Domus_Aurea" title="Domus Aurea">Domus Aurea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pantheon,_Rome" title="Pantheon, Rome">Pantheon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trajan%27s_Column" title="Trajan's Column">Trajan's Column</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trajan%27s_Market" title="Trajan's Market">Trajan's Market</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Catacombs_of_Rome" title="Catacombs of Rome">Catacombs</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Circus_Maximus" title="Circus Maximus">Circus Maximus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baths_of_Caracalla" title="Baths of Caracalla">Baths of Caracalla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castel_Sant%27Angelo" title="Castel Sant'Angelo">Castel Sant'Angelo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mausoleum_of_Augustus" title="Mausoleum of Augustus">Mausoleum of Augustus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ara_Pacis" title="Ara Pacis">Ara Pacis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arch_of_Constantine" title="Arch of Constantine">Arch of Constantine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_of_Cestius" title="Pyramid of Cestius">Pyramid of Cestius</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bocca_della_Verit%C3%A0" title="Bocca della Verità">Bocca della Verità</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval">Medieval</span></h4>
<p>The medieval popular quarters of the city, situated mainly around the Capitol, were largely demolished between the end of the 19th century and the fascist period, but many notable buildings still remain. Basilicas dating from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Christianity" title="Early Christianity">Christian antiquity</a> include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basilica_di_Santa_Maria_Maggiore" title="Basilica di Santa Maria Maggiore">Saint Mary Major</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Saint_Paul_Outside_the_Walls" title="Basilica of Saint Paul Outside the Walls">Saint Paul outside the Walls</a> (the latter largely rebuilt in the 19th century), both housing precious fourth century AD mosaics. Notable later medieval mosaics and frescoes can be also found in the churches of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_in_Trastevere" title="Santa Maria in Trastevere">Santa Maria in Trastevere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santi_Quattro_Coronati" title="Santi Quattro Coronati">Santi Quattro Coronati</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Prassede" title="Santa Prassede">Santa Prassede</a>. Secular buildings include a number of towers, the largest being the <a href="/wiki/Torre_delle_Milizie" title="Torre delle Milizie">Torre delle Milizie</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Torre_dei_Conti" title="Torre dei Conti">Torre dei Conti</a>, both next to the Roman Forum, and the huge outdoor stairway leading up to the basilica of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_in_Aracoeli" title="Santa Maria in Aracoeli">Santa Maria in Aracoeli</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Renaissance_and_Baroque">Renaissance and Baroque</span></h4>
<p>Rome was a major world centre of the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, second only to Florence, and was profoundly affected by the movement. Among others, a masterpiece of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance architecture</a> in Rome is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piazza_del_Campidoglio" title="Piazza del Campidoglio">Piazza del Campidoglio</a> by <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">Michelangelo</a>. During this period, the great aristocratic families of Rome used to build opulent dwellings as the <a href="/wiki/Quirinal_Palace" title="Quirinal Palace">Palazzo del Quirinale</a> (now seat of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Italy" title="President of Italy">President of the Italian Republic</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Venezia" title="Palazzo Venezia">Palazzo Venezia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Farnese" title="Palazzo Farnese">Palazzo Farnese</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Barberini" title="Palazzo Barberini">Palazzo Barberini</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palazzo_Chigi" title="Palazzo Chigi">Palazzo Chigi</a> (now seat of the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Italy" title="Prime Minister of Italy">Italian Prime Minister</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Spada" title="Palazzo Spada">Palazzo Spada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_della_Cancelleria" title="Palazzo della Cancelleria">Palazzo della Cancelleria</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Villa_Farnesina" title="Villa Farnesina">Villa Farnesina</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Piazza_del_Campidoglio_panoramic_view_39948px.jpg" title="Panoramic view of Piazza del Campidoglio, with a copy of the Equestrian Statue of Marcus Aurelius"><img alt="" data-file-height="9734" data-file-width="39948" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Piazza_del_Campidoglio_panoramic_view_39948px.jpg/800px-Piazza_del_Campidoglio_panoramic_view_39948px.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Piazza_del_Campidoglio_panoramic_view_39948px.jpg/1200px-Piazza_del_Campidoglio_panoramic_view_39948px.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Piazza_del_Campidoglio_panoramic_view_39948px.jpg/1600px-Piazza_del_Campidoglio_panoramic_view_39948px.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Piazza_del_Campidoglio_panoramic_view_39948px.jpg" title="File:Piazza del Campidoglio panoramic view 39948px.jpg"> </a></div>Panoramic view of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piazza_del_Campidoglio" title="Piazza del Campidoglio">Piazza del Campidoglio</a>, with a copy of the <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_Statue_of_Marcus_Aurelius" title="Equestrian Statue of Marcus Aurelius">Equestrian Statue of Marcus Aurelius</a></div></div></div>
<p>Many of the famous city's squares – some huge, majestic and often adorned with <a href="/wiki/List_of_obelisks_in_Rome" title="List of obelisks in Rome">obelisks</a>, some small and picturesque – took their present shape during the Renaissance and Baroque periods. The principal ones are <a href="/wiki/Piazza_Navona" title="Piazza Navona">Piazza Navona</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Steps" title="Spanish Steps">Spanish Steps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campo_de%27_Fiori" title="Campo de' Fiori">Campo de' Fiori</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piazza_Venezia" title="Piazza Venezia">Piazza Venezia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palazzo_Farnese,_Rome" title="Palazzo Farnese, Rome">Piazza Farnese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pantheon,_Rome" title="Pantheon, Rome">Piazza della Rotonda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_sopra_Minerva" title="Santa Maria sopra Minerva">Piazza della Minerva</a>. One of the most emblematic examples of Baroque art is the <a href="/wiki/Trevi_Fountain" title="Trevi Fountain">Trevi Fountain</a> by <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Salvi" title="Nicola Salvi">Nicola Salvi</a>. Other notable 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">baroque palaces</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Madama,_Rome" title="Palazzo Madama, Rome">Palazzo Madama</a>, now the seat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Senate" title="Italian Senate">Italian Senate</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Montecitorio" title="Palazzo Montecitorio">Palazzo Montecitorio</a>, now the seat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Chamber_of_Deputies" title="Italian Chamber of Deputies">Chamber of Deputies of Italy</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Neoclassicism">Neoclassicism</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VittioriEmanuele.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/VittioriEmanuele.jpg/220px-VittioriEmanuele.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/VittioriEmanuele.jpg/330px-VittioriEmanuele.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/VittioriEmanuele.jpg/440px-VittioriEmanuele.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VittioriEmanuele.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Victor_Emmanuel_II_Monument" title="Victor Emmanuel II Monument">Victor Emmanuel II Monument</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1870, Rome became the capital city of the new <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a>. During this time, <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neoclassicism</a>, a building style influenced by the architecture of <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">antiquity</a>, became the predominant influence in Roman architecture. During this period, many great palaces in neoclassical styles were built to host ministries, embassies, and other government agencies. One of the best-known symbols of Roman neoclassicism is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monument_to_Vittorio_Emanuele_II" title="Monument to Vittorio Emanuele II">Monument to Vittorio Emanuele II</a> or "Altar of the Fatherland", where the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monument_to_Vittorio_Emanuele_II#Tomb_of_Unknown_Soldier" title="Monument to Vittorio Emanuele II">Grave of the Unknown Soldier</a>, who represents the 650,000 Italian soldiers who died in World War I, is located.
</p>
