<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fascist_architecture">Fascist architecture</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fascist_architecture" title="Fascist architecture">Fascist architecture</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_della_civilt%C3%A0_del_lavoro_(EUR,_Rome)_(5904657870).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Palazzo_della_civilt%C3%A0_del_lavoro_%28EUR%2C_Rome%29_%285904657870%29.jpg/220px-Palazzo_della_civilt%C3%A0_del_lavoro_%28EUR%2C_Rome%29_%285904657870%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Palazzo_della_civilt%C3%A0_del_lavoro_%28EUR%2C_Rome%29_%285904657870%29.jpg/330px-Palazzo_della_civilt%C3%A0_del_lavoro_%28EUR%2C_Rome%29_%285904657870%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Palazzo_della_civilt%C3%A0_del_lavoro_%28EUR%2C_Rome%29_%285904657870%29.jpg/440px-Palazzo_della_civilt%C3%A0_del_lavoro_%28EUR%2C_Rome%29_%285904657870%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_della_civilt%C3%A0_del_lavoro_(EUR,_Rome)_(5904657870).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_della_Civilt%C3%A0_Italiana" title="Palazzo della Civiltà Italiana">Palazzo della Civiltà Italiana</a> in EUR district</div></div></div>
<p>The Fascist regime that ruled in Italy between 1922 and 1943 had its showcase in Rome. Mussolini ordered the construction of new roads and piazzas, resulting in the destruction of older roads, houses, churches and palaces erected during papal rule. The main activities during his government were: the "isolation" of the <a href="/wiki/Capitoline_Hill" title="Capitoline Hill">Capitoline Hill</a>; Via dei Monti, later renamed Via del'Impero, and finally <a href="/wiki/Via_dei_Fori_Imperiali" title="Via dei Fori Imperiali">Via dei Fori Imperiali</a>; Via del Mare, later renamed Via del <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teatro_di_Marcello" title="Teatro di Marcello">Teatro di Marcello</a>; the "isolation" of the <a href="/wiki/Mausoleum_of_Augustus" title="Mausoleum of Augustus">Mausoleum of Augustus</a>, with the erection of Piazza Augusto Imperatore; and <a href="/wiki/Via_della_Conciliazione" title="Via della Conciliazione">Via della Conciliazione</a>.
</p><p>Architecturally, Italian Fascism favoured the most modern movements, such as <a href="/wiki/Rationalism_(architecture)" title="Rationalism (architecture)">Rationalism</a>. Parallel to this, in the 1920s another style emerged, named "Stile Novecento", characterised by its links with ancient Roman architecture. Two important complexes in the latter style are the Foro Mussolini, now <a href="/wiki/Foro_Italico" title="Foro Italico">Foro Italico</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Del_Debbio" title="Enrico Del Debbio">Enrico Del Debbio</a>, and the <i>Città universitaria</i> ("University city"), by <a href="/wiki/Marcello_Piacentini" title="Marcello Piacentini">Marcello Piacentini</a>, also author of the controversial destruction of part of the Borgo rione to open Via della Conciliazione.
</p><p>The most important Fascist site in Rome is the <a href="/wiki/EUR,_Rome" title="EUR, Rome">EUR</a> district, designed in 1938 by Piacentini. This new quarter emerged as a compromise between Rationalist and Novecento architects, the former being led by <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Pagano" title="Giuseppe Pagano">Giuseppe Pagano</a>. The EUR was originally conceived for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esposizione_universale_(1942)" title="Esposizione universale (1942)">1942 world exhibition</a>, and was called "E.42" (<i>"Esposizione 42"</i>). The most representative buildings of EUR are the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_della_Civilt%C3%A0_Italiana" title="Palazzo della Civiltà Italiana">Palazzo della Civiltà Italiana</a> (1938–1943), and the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_dei_Congressi" title="Palazzo dei Congressi">Palazzo dei Congressi</a>, examples of the Rationalist style. The world exhibition never took place, because Italy entered the Second World War in 1940, and the buildings were partly destroyed in 1943 in fighting between the Italian and German armies and later abandoned. The quarter was restored in the 1950s when the Roman authorities found that they already had the seed of an off-centre business district of the type that other capitals were still planning (<a href="/wiki/London_Docklands" title="London Docklands">London Docklands</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_D%C3%A9fense" title="La Défense">La Défense</a> in Paris). Also, the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_della_Farnesina" title="Palazzo della Farnesina">Palazzo della Farnesina</a>, the current seat of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Italy)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Italy)">Italian Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>, was designed in 1935 in pure Fascist style.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_gardens">Parks and gardens</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_parks_and_gardens_in_Rome" title="List of parks and gardens in Rome">List of parks and gardens in Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rome-VillaBorghese-TempleEsculape.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2382" data-file-width="3176" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Rome-VillaBorghese-TempleEsculape.jpg/220px-Rome-VillaBorghese-TempleEsculape.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Rome-VillaBorghese-TempleEsculape.jpg/330px-Rome-VillaBorghese-TempleEsculape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Rome-VillaBorghese-TempleEsculape.jpg/440px-Rome-VillaBorghese-TempleEsculape.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rome-VillaBorghese-TempleEsculape.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Aesculapius_(Villa_Borghese)" title="Temple of Aesculapius (Villa Borghese)">Temple of Aesculapius</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Villa_Borghese_gardens" title="Villa Borghese gardens">Villa Borghese gardens</a></div></div></div>
<p>Public parks and nature reserves cover a large area in Rome, and the city has one of the largest areas of green space among European capitals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[113]</a></sup> The most notable part of this green space is represented by the large number of villas and landscaped gardens created by the Italian aristocracy. While most of the parks surrounding the villas were destroyed during the building boom of the late 19th century, some of them remain. The most notable of these are the <a href="/wiki/Villa_Borghese_gardens" title="Villa Borghese gardens">Villa Borghese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Villa_Ada" title="Villa Ada">Villa Ada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Villa_Doria_Pamphili" title="Villa Doria Pamphili">Villa Doria Pamphili</a>. Villa Doria Pamphili is west of the Gianicolo hill, comprising some 1.8 km<sup>2</sup> (0.7 <a href="/wiki/Square_mile" title="Square mile">sq mi</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Villa_Sciarra_(Rome)" title="Villa Sciarra (Rome)">Villa Sciarra</a> is on the hill, with playgrounds for children and shaded walking areas. In the nearby area of Trastevere, the <a href="/wiki/Orto_Botanico_dell%27Universit%C3%A0_di_Roma_%22La_Sapienza%22" title="Orto Botanico dell'Università di Roma &quot;La Sapienza&quot;">Orto Botanico</a> (Botanical Garden) is a cool and shady green space. The old Roman hippodrome (Circus Maximus) is another large green space: it has few trees but is overlooked by the Palatine and the Rose Garden ('roseto comunale'). Nearby is the lush <a href="/wiki/Villa_Celimontana" title="Villa Celimontana">Villa Celimontana</a>, close to the gardens surrounding the Baths of Caracalla. The Villa Borghese garden is the best known large green space in Rome, with famous art galleries among its shaded walks. Overlooking <a href="/wiki/Piazza_del_Popolo" title="Piazza del Popolo">Piazza del Popolo</a> and the Spanish Steps are the gardens of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pincio" title="Pincio">Pincio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Villa_Medici" title="Villa Medici">Villa Medici</a>. There is also a notable pine wood at <a href="/wiki/Castelfusano" title="Castelfusano">Castelfusano</a>, near Ostia. Rome also has a number of regional parks of much more recent origin, including the <a href="/wiki/Pineto_Regional_Park" title="Pineto Regional Park">Pineto Regional Park</a> and the Appian Way Regional Park. There are also nature reserves at Marcigliana and at Tenuta di Castelporziano.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fountains_and_aqueducts">Fountains and aqueducts</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_fountains_in_Rome" title="List of fountains in Rome">List of fountains in Rome</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_aqueducts_in_the_city_of_Rome" title="List of aqueducts in the city of Rome">List of aqueducts in the city of Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trevi_Fountain,_Rome,_Italy_2_-_May_2007.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2325" data-file-width="3500" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Trevi_Fountain%2C_Rome%2C_Italy_2_-_May_2007.jpg/220px-Trevi_Fountain%2C_Rome%2C_Italy_2_-_May_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Trevi_Fountain%2C_Rome%2C_Italy_2_-_May_2007.jpg/330px-Trevi_Fountain%2C_Rome%2C_Italy_2_-_May_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Trevi_Fountain%2C_Rome%2C_Italy_2_-_May_2007.jpg/440px-Trevi_Fountain%2C_Rome%2C_Italy_2_-_May_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trevi_Fountain,_Rome,_Italy_2_-_May_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Trevi_Fountain" title="Trevi Fountain">Trevi Fountain</a>. Construction began during the time of Ancient Rome and was completed in 1762 by a design of <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Salvi" title="Nicola Salvi">Nicola Salvi</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Rome is a city famous for its numerous fountains, built-in all different styles, from Classical and Medieval, to Baroque and Neoclassical. The city has had <a href="/wiki/Fountain" title="Fountain">fountains</a> for more than two thousand years, and they have provided drinking water and decorated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piazza" title="Piazza">piazzas</a> of Rome. During the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, in 98 AD, according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sextus_Julius_Frontinus" title="Sextus Julius Frontinus">Sextus Julius Frontinus</a>, the Roman consul who was named <i><a href="/wiki/Curator_Aquarum" title="Curator Aquarum">curator aquarum</a></i> or guardian of the water of the city, Rome had nine <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(watercourse)" title="Aqueduct (watercourse)">aqueducts</a> which fed 39 monumental fountains and 591 public basins, not counting the water supplied to the Imperial household, baths, and owners of private villas. Each of the major fountains was connected to two different aqueducts, in case one was shut down for service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 17th and 18th century, the Roman popes reconstructed other ruined Roman aqueducts and built new display fountains to mark their termini, launching the golden age of the Roman fountain. The fountains of Rome, like the paintings of <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">Rubens</a>, were expressions of the new style of Baroque art. They were crowded with allegorical figures and filled with emotion and movement. In these fountains, sculpture became the principal element, and the water was used simply to animate and decorate the sculptures. They, like baroque gardens, were "a visual representation of confidence and power".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[115]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statues">Statues</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Talking_statues_of_Rome" title="Talking statues of Rome">Talking statues of Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vierstr%C3%B6mebrunnen-Fontana_dei_Quattro_Fiumi_(27903447766).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1664" data-file-width="2496" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vierstr%C3%B6mebrunnen-Fontana_dei_Quattro_Fiumi_%2827903447766%29.jpg/220px-Vierstr%C3%B6mebrunnen-Fontana_dei_Quattro_Fiumi_%2827903447766%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vierstr%C3%B6mebrunnen-Fontana_dei_Quattro_Fiumi_%2827903447766%29.jpg/330px-Vierstr%C3%B6mebrunnen-Fontana_dei_Quattro_Fiumi_%2827903447766%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vierstr%C3%B6mebrunnen-Fontana_dei_Quattro_Fiumi_%2827903447766%29.jpg/440px-Vierstr%C3%B6mebrunnen-Fontana_dei_Quattro_Fiumi_%2827903447766%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vierstr%C3%B6mebrunnen-Fontana_dei_Quattro_Fiumi_(27903447766).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fontana dei Fiumi by <a href="/wiki/Gian_Lorenzo_Bernini" title="Gian Lorenzo Bernini">Gian Lorenzo Bernini</a>, 1648</div></div></div>
<p>Rome is well known for its statues but, in particular, the <a href="/wiki/Talking_statues_of_Rome" title="Talking statues of Rome">talking statues of Rome</a>. These are usually ancient statues which have become popular soapboxes for political and social discussion, and places for people to (often satirically) voice their opinions. There are two main talking statues: the <a href="/wiki/Pasquino" title="Pasquino">Pasquino</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Marforio" title="Marforio">Marforio</a>, yet there are four other noted ones: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Il_Babuino" title="Il Babuino">il Babuino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madama_Lucrezia" title="Madama Lucrezia">Madama Lucrezia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Il_Facchino" title="Il Facchino">il Facchino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abbot_Luigi" title="Abbot Luigi">Abbot Luigi</a>. Most of these statues are ancient Roman or classical, and most of them also depict mythical gods, ancient people or legendary figures; il Pasquino represents <a href="/wiki/Menelaus" title="Menelaus">Menelaus</a>, Abbot Luigi is an unknown Roman magistrate, il Babuino is supposed to be <a href="/wiki/Silenus" title="Silenus">Silenus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marforio" title="Marforio">Marforio</a> represents <a href="/wiki/Oceanus" title="Oceanus">Oceanus</a>, Madama Lucrezia is a bust of <a href="/wiki/Isis" title="Isis">Isis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Il_Facchino" title="Il Facchino">il Facchino</a> is the only non-Roman statue, created in 1580, and not representing anyone in particular. They are often, due to their status, covered with placards or <a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">graffiti</a> expressing political ideas and points of view. Other statues in the city, which are not related to the talking statues, include those of the Ponte Sant'Angelo, or several monuments scattered across the city, such as that to <a href="/wiki/Giordano_Bruno" title="Giordano Bruno">Giordano Bruno</a> in the Campo de'Fiori.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Obelisks_and_columns">Obelisks and columns</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_obelisks_in_Rome" title="List of obelisks in Rome">List of obelisks in Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Piazza_del_Popolo_Obelisco_Flaminio_a_Roma.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4912" data-file-width="7360" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Piazza_del_Popolo_Obelisco_Flaminio_a_Roma.jpg/220px-Piazza_del_Popolo_Obelisco_Flaminio_a_Roma.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Piazza_del_Popolo_Obelisco_Flaminio_a_Roma.jpg/330px-Piazza_del_Popolo_Obelisco_Flaminio_a_Roma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Piazza_del_Popolo_Obelisco_Flaminio_a_Roma.jpg/440px-Piazza_del_Popolo_Obelisco_Flaminio_a_Roma.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Piazza_del_Popolo_Obelisco_Flaminio_a_Roma.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Flaminio_Obelisk" title="Flaminio Obelisk">Flaminio Obelisk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piazza_del_Popolo" title="Piazza del Popolo">Piazza del Popolo</a></div></div></div>
<p>The city hosts eight <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egyptian</a> and five <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">ancient Roman</a> <a href="/wiki/Obelisk" title="Obelisk">obelisks</a>, together with a number of more modern obelisks; there was also formerly (until 2005) an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aksumite_Empire" title="Aksumite Empire">ancient Ethiopian</a> obelisk in Rome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[116]</a></sup> The city contains some of obelisks in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piazza" title="Piazza">piazzas</a>, such as in <a href="/wiki/Piazza_Navona" title="Piazza Navona">Piazza Navona</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Peter%27s_Square" title="Saint Peter's Square">St Peter's Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piazza_di_Monte_Citorio" title="Piazza di Monte Citorio">Piazza Montecitorio</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Piazza_del_Popolo" title="Piazza del Popolo">Piazza del Popolo</a>, and others in <a href="/wiki/Villa" title="Villa">villas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thermae" title="Thermae">thermae</a> parks and gardens, such as in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Villa_Mattei" title="Villa Mattei">Villa Celimontana</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baths_of_Diocletian" title="Baths of Diocletian">Baths of Diocletian</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pincian_Hill" title="Pincian Hill">Pincian Hill</a>. Moreover, the centre of Rome hosts also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trajan%27s_column" title="Trajan's column">Trajan</a>'s and <a href="/wiki/Column_of_Marcus_Aurelius" title="Column of Marcus Aurelius">Antonine Column</a>, two ancient Roman columns with spiral relief. The Column of Marcus Aurelius is located in <a href="/wiki/Piazza_Colonna" title="Piazza Colonna">Piazza Colonna</a> and it was built around 180 AD by <a href="/wiki/Commodus" title="Commodus">Commodus</a> in memory of his parents. The <a href="/wiki/Column_of_Marcus_Aurelius" title="Column of Marcus Aurelius">Column of Marcus Aurelius</a> was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Trajan%27s_Column" title="Trajan's Column">Trajan's Column</a> at <a href="/wiki/Trajan%27s_Forum" title="Trajan's Forum">Trajan's Forum</a>, which is part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Fora" title="Imperial Fora">Imperial Fora</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bridges">Bridges</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_bridges_in_Rome" title="List of bridges in Rome">List of bridges in Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bridge_Vittorio_Emanuele_II_at_sunset.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3848" data-file-width="5716" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bridge_Vittorio_Emanuele_II_at_sunset.jpg/220px-Bridge_Vittorio_Emanuele_II_at_sunset.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bridge_Vittorio_Emanuele_II_at_sunset.jpg/330px-Bridge_Vittorio_Emanuele_II_at_sunset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bridge_Vittorio_Emanuele_II_at_sunset.jpg/440px-Bridge_Vittorio_Emanuele_II_at_sunset.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bridge_Vittorio_Emanuele_II_at_sunset.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ponte_Vittorio_Emanuele_II" title="Ponte Vittorio Emanuele II">Ponte Vittorio Emanuele II</a> at sunset</div></div></div>
<p>The city of Rome contains numerous famous bridges which cross the <a href="/wiki/Tiber" title="Tiber">Tiber</a>. The only bridge to remain unaltered until today from the classical age is <a href="/wiki/Pons_Fabricius" title="Pons Fabricius">Ponte dei Quattro Capi</a>, which connects the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isola_Tiberina" title="Isola Tiberina">Isola Tiberina</a> with the left bank. The other surviving – albeit modified – ancient Roman bridges crossing the Tiber are <a href="/wiki/Pons_Cestius" title="Pons Cestius">Ponte Cestio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ponte_Sant%27Angelo" title="Ponte Sant'Angelo">Ponte Sant'Angelo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ponte_Milvio" title="Ponte Milvio">Ponte Milvio</a>. Considering <a href="/wiki/Ponte_Nomentano" title="Ponte Nomentano">Ponte Nomentano</a>, also built during ancient Rome, which crosses the <a href="/wiki/Aniene" title="Aniene">Aniene</a>, currently there are five ancient Roman bridges still remaining in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[118]</a></sup> Other noteworthy bridges are <a href="/wiki/Ponte_Sisto" title="Ponte Sisto">Ponte Sisto</a>, the first bridge built in the Renaissance above Roman foundations; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ponte_Rotto" title="Ponte Rotto">Ponte Rotto</a>, actually the only remaining arch of the ancient <i>Pons Aemilius</i>, collapsed during the flood of 1598 and demolished at the end of the 19th century; and <a href="/wiki/Ponte_Vittorio_Emanuele_II" title="Ponte Vittorio Emanuele II">Ponte Vittorio Emanuele II</a>, a modern bridge connecting Corso Vittorio Emanuele and Borgo. Most of the city's public bridges were built in Classical or Renaissance style, but also in Baroque, Neoclassical and Modern styles. According to the <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a>, the finest ancient bridge remaining in Rome is the <a href="/wiki/Ponte_Sant%27Angelo" title="Ponte Sant'Angelo">Ponte Sant'Angelo</a>, which was completed in 135 AD, and was decorated with ten statues of the angels, designed by <a href="/wiki/Gian_Lorenzo_Bernini" title="Gian Lorenzo Bernini">Bernini</a> in 1688.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Catacombs">Catacombs</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Catacombs_of_Rome" title="Catacombs of Rome">Catacombs of Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PiusXItomb2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/PiusXItomb2.jpg/220px-PiusXItomb2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/PiusXItomb2.jpg/330px-PiusXItomb2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/PiusXItomb2.jpg/440px-PiusXItomb2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PiusXItomb2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Necropolis" title="Vatican Necropolis">Vatican Caves</a>, the place where many popes are buried</div></div></div>
<p>Rome has an extensive amount of ancient catacombs, or underground burial places under or near the city, of which there are at least forty, some discovered only in recent decades. Though most famous for Christian burials, they include <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_ancient_Rome" title="Religion in ancient Rome">pagan</a> and Jewish burials, either in separate catacombs or mixed together. The first large-scale catacombs were excavated from the 2nd century onwards. Originally they were carved through <a href="/wiki/Tuff" title="Tuff">tuff</a>, a soft <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_rock" title="Volcanic rock">volcanic rock</a>, outside the boundaries of the city, because <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman law</a> forbade burial places within city limits. Currently, maintenance of the catacombs is in the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Papacy</a> which has invested in the <a href="/wiki/Salesians_of_Don_Bosco" title="Salesians of Don Bosco">Salesians of Don Bosco</a> the supervision of the Catacombs of St. Callixtus on the outskirts of Rome.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<p>As the capital of Italy, Rome hosts all the principal institutions of the nation, including the Presidency of the Republic, the government (and its single <span title="Italian-language text"><i lang="it">Ministeri</i></span>), the Parliament, the main judicial Courts, and the diplomatic representatives of all the countries for the states of Italy and Vatican City. Many international institutions are located in Rome, notably cultural and scientific ones, such as the American Institute, the British School, the French Academy, the Scandinavian Institutes, and the German Archaeological Institute. There are also specialised agencies of the United Nations, such as the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> (FAO). Rome also hosts major international and worldwide political and cultural organisations, such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Fund_for_Agricultural_Development" title="International Fund for Agricultural Development">International Fund for Agricultural Development</a> (IFAD), <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> (WFP), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NATO_Defence_College" title="NATO Defence College">NATO Defence College</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Centre_for_the_Study_of_the_Preservation_and_Restoration_of_Cultural_Property" title="International Centre for the Study of the Preservation and Restoration of Cultural Property">International Centre for the Study of the Preservation and Restoration of Cultural Property</a> (ICCROM).
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panoramic_view_of_EUR_business_district,_Rome.jpg" title="Panoramic view of the EUR business district"><img alt="" data-file-height="558" data-file-width="2363" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Panoramic_view_of_EUR_business_district%2C_Rome.jpg/800px-Panoramic_view_of_EUR_business_district%2C_Rome.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Panoramic_view_of_EUR_business_district%2C_Rome.jpg/1200px-Panoramic_view_of_EUR_business_district%2C_Rome.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Panoramic_view_of_EUR_business_district%2C_Rome.jpg/1600px-Panoramic_view_of_EUR_business_district%2C_Rome.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panoramic_view_of_EUR_business_district,_Rome.jpg" title="File:Panoramic view of EUR business district, Rome.jpg"> </a></div>Panoramic view of the <a href="/wiki/EUR,_Rome" title="EUR, Rome">EUR</a> business district</div></div></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Global_city#GaWC_study" title="Global city">GaWC study of world cities</a>, Rome is a "Beta +" city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GAWC_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-GAWC-123">[120]</a></sup> The city was ranked in 2014 as 32nd in the Global Cities Index, the highest in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atkearney.at_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-atkearney.at-124">[121]</a></sup> With a 2005 GDP of €94.376 billion (US$121.5 billion),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rapporto2006_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-rapporto2006-125">[122]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (May 2018)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> the city produces 6.7% of the national GDP (more than any other single city in Italy), and its unemployment rate, lowered from 11.1% to 6.5% between 2001 and 2005, is now one of the lowest rates of all the European Union capital cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rapporto2006_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-rapporto2006-125">[122]</a></sup> Rome's economy grows at around 4.4% annually and continues to grow at a higher rate in comparison to any other city in the rest of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rapporto2006_125-2"><a href="#cite_note-rapporto2006-125">[122]</a></sup> This means that were Rome a country, it would be the world's 52nd richest country by GDP, near to the size to that of Egypt. Rome also had a 2003 GDP per capita of €29,153 (US$37,412), which was second in Italy, (after Milan), and is more than 134.1% of the EU average GDP per capita.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-observatoribarcelona.org_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-observatoribarcelona.org-126">[123]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (May 2018)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> Rome, on the whole, has the highest total earnings in Italy, reaching €47,076,890,463 in 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilsole24ore.com_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-ilsole24ore.com-127">[124]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (May 2018)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> yet, in terms of average workers' incomes, the city places itself 9th in Italy, with €24,509.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilsole24ore.com_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-ilsole24ore.com-127">[124]</a></sup> On a global level, Rome's workers receive the 30th highest wages in 2009, coming three places higher than in 2008, in which the city ranked 33rd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citymayors_a_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-citymayors_a-128">[125]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (May 2018)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> The Rome area had a <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">GDP amounting to $167.8 billion</a>, and $38,765 per capita.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brookings_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brookings-129">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Temple_of_Hadrian.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1356" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Temple_of_Hadrian.jpg/220px-Temple_of_Hadrian.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Temple_of_Hadrian.jpg/330px-Temple_of_Hadrian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Temple_of_Hadrian.jpg/440px-Temple_of_Hadrian.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Temple_of_Hadrian.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rome chamber of commerce in the ancient <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Hadrian" title="Temple of Hadrian">Temple of Hadrian</a></div></div></div>
<p>Although the economy of Rome is characterised by the absence of heavy industry, and it is largely dominated by <a href="/wiki/Service_(economics)" title="Service (economics)">services</a>, high-technology companies (IT, aerospace, defence, telecommunications), research, construction and commercial activities (especially banking), and the huge development of tourism are very dynamic and extremely important to its economy. Rome's international airport, <a href="/wiki/Fiumicino" title="Fiumicino">Fiumicino</a>, is the largest in Italy, and the city hosts the head offices of the vast majority of the major Italian companies, as well as the headquarters of three of the world's 100 largest companies: <a href="/wiki/Enel" title="Enel">Enel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eni" title="Eni">Eni</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telecom_Italia" title="Telecom Italia">Telecom Italia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forbes_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-130">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>Universities, national radio and television and the movie industry in Rome are also important parts of the economy: Rome is also the hub of the <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Italy" title="Cinema of Italy">Italian film industry</a>, thanks to the Cinecittà studios, working since the 1930s. The city is also a centre for banking and insurance as well as electronics, energy, transport, and aerospace industries. Numerous international companies and agencies headquarters, government ministries, conference centres, sports venues, and museums are located in Rome's principal business districts: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esposizione_Universale_Roma" title="Esposizione Universale Roma">Esposizione Universale Roma</a> (EUR); the <i>Torrino</i> (further south from the EUR); the <i>Magliana</i>; the <i>Parco de' Medici-Laurentina</i> and the so-called <i>Tiburtina-valley</i> along the ancient <a href="/wiki/Via_Tiburtina" title="Via Tiburtina">Via Tiburtina</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sapienza_entrance_(20040201351).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sapienza_entrance_%2820040201351%29.jpg/220px-Sapienza_entrance_%2820040201351%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sapienza_entrance_%2820040201351%29.jpg/330px-Sapienza_entrance_%2820040201351%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sapienza_entrance_%2820040201351%29.jpg/440px-Sapienza_entrance_%2820040201351%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sapienza_entrance_(20040201351).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Sapienza_University_of_Rome" title="Sapienza University of Rome">Sapienza University of Rome</a>, founded in 1303</div></div></div>
<p>Rome is a nationwide and major international centre for higher education, containing numerous academies, colleges and universities. It boasts a large variety of academies and colleges, and has always been a major worldwide intellectual and educational centre, especially during <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, along with Florence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[128]</a></sup> According to the City Brands Index, Rome is considered the world's second most historically, educationally and culturally interesting and beautiful city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rome has many universities and colleges. Its first university, <a href="/wiki/Sapienza_University_of_Rome" title="Sapienza University of Rome">La Sapienza</a> (founded in 1303), is one of the largest in the world, with more than 140,000 students attending; in 2005 it ranked as Europe's 33rd best university<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[130]</a></sup> and in 2013 the Sapienza University of Rome ranked as the 62nd in the world and the top in Italy in its <i>World University Rankings</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[131]</a></sup> and has been ranked among Europe's 50 and the world's 150 best colleges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[132]</a></sup> In order to decrease the overcrowding of La Sapienza, two new public universities were founded during the last decades: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Rome_Tor_Vergata" title="University of Rome Tor Vergata">Tor Vergata</a> in 1982, and <a href="/wiki/Roma_Tre_University" title="Roma Tre University">Roma Tre</a> in 1992. Rome hosts also the LUISS School of Government,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[133]</a></sup> Italy's most important graduate university in the areas of international affairs and European studies as well as <a href="/wiki/LUISS_Business_School" title="LUISS Business School">LUISS Business School</a>, Italy's most important business school. Rome <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Istituto_superiore_per_le_industrie_artistiche_(ISIA)" title="Istituto superiore per le industrie artistiche (ISIA)">ISIA</a> was founded in 1973 by <a href="/wiki/Giulio_Carlo_Argan" title="Giulio Carlo Argan">Giulio Carlo Argan</a> and is Italy's oldest institution in the field of <a href="/wiki/Industrial_design" title="Industrial design">industrial design</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_Casanatense.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1081" data-file-width="1649" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Biblioteca_Casanatense.jpg/220px-Biblioteca_Casanatense.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Biblioteca_Casanatense.jpg/330px-Biblioteca_Casanatense.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Biblioteca_Casanatense.jpg/440px-Biblioteca_Casanatense.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_Casanatense.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_Casanatense" title="Biblioteca Casanatense">Biblioteca Casanatense</a></div></div></div>
<p>Rome contains many <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_university" title="Pontifical university">pontifical universities</a> and other institutes, including the <a href="/wiki/British_School_at_Rome" title="British School at Rome">British School at Rome</a>, the <a href="/wiki/French_Academy_in_Rome" title="French Academy in Rome">French School in Rome</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Gregorian_University" title="Pontifical Gregorian University">Pontifical Gregorian University</a> (the oldest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> university in the world, founded in 1551), <a href="/wiki/Istituto_Europeo_di_Design" title="Istituto Europeo di Design">Istituto Europeo di Design</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_de%27_Medici_School" title="Lorenzo de' Medici School">Scuola Lorenzo de' Medici</a>, the Link <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Link_Campus" title="Link Campus">Campus of Malta</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A0_Campus_Bio-Medico" title="Università Campus Bio-Medico">Università Campus Bio-Medico</a>. Rome is also the location of two American Universities; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_American_University_of_Rome" title="The American University of Rome">The American University of Rome</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[134]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot_University" title="John Cabot University">John Cabot University</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_University_(Italy)" title="St. John's University (Italy)">St. John's University</a> branch campus, <a href="/wiki/John_Felice_Rome_Center" title="John Felice Rome Center">John Felice Rome Center</a>, a campus of <a href="/wiki/Loyola_University_Chicago" title="Loyola University Chicago">Loyola University Chicago</a> and Temple University Rome, a campus of <a href="/wiki/Temple_University" title="Temple University">Temple University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[135]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Colleges" title="Roman Colleges">Roman Colleges</a> are several <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">seminaries</a> for students from foreign countries studying for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_priesthood" title="Catholic priesthood">priesthood</a> at the Pontifical Universities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAC_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAC-139">[136]</a></sup>
Examples include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venerable_English_College" title="Venerable English College">Venerable English College</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_North_American_College" title="Pontifical North American College">Pontifical North American College</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Scots_College_(Rome)" title="Scots College (Rome)">Scots College</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Croatian_College_of_St._Jerome" title="Pontifical Croatian College of St. Jerome">Pontifical Croatian College of St. Jerome</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_nazionale_centrale_di_Roma.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Biblioteca_nazionale_centrale_di_Roma.jpg/220px-Biblioteca_nazionale_centrale_di_Roma.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Biblioteca_nazionale_centrale_di_Roma.jpg/330px-Biblioteca_nazionale_centrale_di_Roma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Biblioteca_nazionale_centrale_di_Roma.jpg/440px-Biblioteca_nazionale_centrale_di_Roma.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biblioteca_nazionale_centrale_di_Roma.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Central_Library_(Rome)" title="National Central Library (Rome)">National Central Library</a></div></div></div>
<p>Rome's major libraries include: the <a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_Angelica" title="Biblioteca Angelica">Biblioteca Angelica</a>, opened in 1604, making it Italy's first public library; the <a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_Vallicelliana" title="Biblioteca Vallicelliana">Biblioteca Vallicelliana</a>, established in 1565; the <a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_Casanatense" title="Biblioteca Casanatense">Biblioteca Casanatense</a>, opened in 1701; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Central_Library_(Rome)" title="National Central Library (Rome)">National Central Library</a>, one of the two national libraries in Italy, which contains 4,126,002 volumes; The Biblioteca del Ministero degli Affari Esteri, specialised in diplomacy, foreign affairs and modern history; the Biblioteca dell'Istituto dell'Enciclopedia Italiana; the Biblioteca Don Bosco, one of the largest and most modern of all Salesian libraries; the Biblioteca e Museo teatrale del Burcardo, a museum-library specialised in history of drama and theatre; the Biblioteca della <a href="/wiki/Societ%C3%A0_Geografica_Italiana" title="Società Geografica Italiana">Società Geografica Italiana</a>, which is based in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Villa_Mattei" title="Villa Mattei">Villa Celimontana</a> and is the most important geographical library in Italy, and one of Europe's most important;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[137]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Library" title="Vatican Library">Vatican Library</a>, one of the oldest and most important libraries in the world, which was formally established in 1475, though in fact much older and has 75,000 <a href="/wiki/Codex" title="Codex">codices</a>, as well as 1.1 million printed books, which include some 8,500 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incunabulum" title="Incunabulum">incunabula</a>. There are also many specialist libraries attached to various foreign cultural institutes in Rome, among them that of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_in_Rome" title="American Academy in Rome">American Academy in Rome</a>, the <a href="/wiki/French_Academy_in_Rome" title="French Academy in Rome">French Academy in Rome</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bibliotheca_Hertziana_%E2%80%93_Max_Planck_Institute_of_Art_History" title="Bibliotheca Hertziana – Max Planck Institute of Art History">Bibliotheca Hertziana – Max Planck Institute of Art History</a>, a German library, often noted for excellence in the arts and sciences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[138]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Culture_in_Rome" title="Culture in Rome">Culture in Rome</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment_and_performing_arts">Entertainment and performing arts</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_in_Rome" title="Music in Rome">Music in Rome</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Events_in_Rome" title="Events in Rome">Events in Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_dell%27Opera_a_Roma.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Teatro_dell%27Opera_a_Roma.JPG/220px-Teatro_dell%27Opera_a_Roma.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Teatro_dell%27Opera_a_Roma.JPG/330px-Teatro_dell%27Opera_a_Roma.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Teatro_dell%27Opera_a_Roma.JPG/440px-Teatro_dell%27Opera_a_Roma.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_dell%27Opera_a_Roma.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Teatro_dell%27Opera_di_Roma" title="Teatro dell'Opera di Roma">Teatro dell'Opera di Roma</a> at the Piazza Beniamino Gigli</div></div></div>
<p>Rome is an important centre for music, and it has an intense musical scene, including several prestigious music conservatories and theatres. It hosts the <a href="/wiki/Accademia_Nazionale_di_Santa_Cecilia" title="Accademia Nazionale di Santa Cecilia">Accademia Nazionale di Santa Cecilia</a> (founded in 1585), for which new concert halls have been built in the new <a href="/wiki/Parco_della_Musica" title="Parco della Musica">Parco della Musica</a>, one of the largest musical venues in the world. Rome also has an opera house, the <a href="/wiki/Teatro_dell%27Opera_di_Roma" title="Teatro dell'Opera di Roma">Teatro dell'Opera di Roma</a>, as well as several minor musical institutions. The city also played host to the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_1991" title="Eurovision Song Contest 1991">Eurovision Song Contest</a> in 1991 and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards_2004" title="MTV Europe Music Awards 2004">MTV Europe Music Awards</a> in 2004.
</p><p>Rome has also had a major impact on music history. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_School" title="Roman School">Roman School</a> was a group of composers of predominantly church music, which were active in the city during the 16th and 17th centuries, therefore spanning the late <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_music" title="Renaissance music">Renaissance</a> and early <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">Baroque</a> eras. The term also refers to the music they produced. Many of the composers had a direct connection to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Vatican</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel" title="Sistine Chapel">papal chapel</a>, though they worked at several churches; stylistically they are often contrasted with the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(music)" title="Venetian School (music)">Venetian School</a> of composers, a concurrent movement which was much more progressive. By far the most famous composer of the Roman School is <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Pierluigi_da_Palestrina" title="Giovanni Pierluigi da Palestrina">Giovanni Pierluigi da Palestrina</a>, whose name has been associated for four hundred years with smooth, clear, <a href="/wiki/Polyphony" title="Polyphony">polyphonic</a> perfection. However, there were other composers working in Rome, and in a variety of styles and forms.
</p><p>Between 1960 and 1970 Rome was considered to be as a “new Hollywood” because of the many actors and directors who worked there; Via Vittorio Veneto had transformed into a glamour place where you could meet famous people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[139]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Rome" title="Tourism in Rome">Tourism in Rome</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_tourist_attractions_in_Rome" title="List of tourist attractions in Rome">List of tourist attractions in Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Piazza_di_Spagna,_Roma_-_scalinata_fc03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Piazza_di_Spagna%2C_Roma_-_scalinata_fc03.jpg/220px-Piazza_di_Spagna%2C_Roma_-_scalinata_fc03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Piazza_di_Spagna%2C_Roma_-_scalinata_fc03.jpg/330px-Piazza_di_Spagna%2C_Roma_-_scalinata_fc03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Piazza_di_Spagna%2C_Roma_-_scalinata_fc03.jpg/440px-Piazza_di_Spagna%2C_Roma_-_scalinata_fc03.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Piazza_di_Spagna,_Roma_-_scalinata_fc03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Steps" title="Spanish Steps">Spanish Steps</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faber_Village,_Lido_di_Ostia_RM,_Lazio,_Italy_-_panoramio_(3).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1890" data-file-width="2835" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Faber_Village%2C_Lido_di_Ostia_RM%2C_Lazio%2C_Italy_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg/220px-Faber_Village%2C_Lido_di_Ostia_RM%2C_Lazio%2C_Italy_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Faber_Village%2C_Lido_di_Ostia_RM%2C_Lazio%2C_Italy_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg/330px-Faber_Village%2C_Lido_di_Ostia_RM%2C_Lazio%2C_Italy_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Faber_Village%2C_Lido_di_Ostia_RM%2C_Lazio%2C_Italy_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg/440px-Faber_Village%2C_Lido_di_Ostia_RM%2C_Lazio%2C_Italy_-_panoramio_%283%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Faber_Village,_Lido_di_Ostia_RM,_Lazio,_Italy_-_panoramio_(3).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ostia_(Rome)" title="Ostia (Rome)">Ostia Lido beach</a></div></div></div>
<p>Rome today is one of the most important tourist destinations of the world, due to the incalculable immensity of its archaeological and artistic treasures, as well as for the charm of its unique traditions, the beauty of its panoramic views, and the majesty of its magnificent "villas" (parks). Among the most significant resources are the many museums – <a href="/wiki/Capitoline_Museums" title="Capitoline Museums">Musei Capitolini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Museums" title="Vatican Museums">the Vatican Museums</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Galleria_Borghese" title="Galleria Borghese">Galleria Borghese</a> and others dedicated to modern and contemporary art – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(watercourse)" title="Aqueduct (watercourse)">aqueducts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fountain" title="Fountain">fountains</a>, churches, <a href="/wiki/Palace" title="Palace">palaces</a>, historical buildings, the <a href="/wiki/Monument" title="Monument">monuments</a> and ruins of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Forum" title="Roman Forum">Roman Forum</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Catacombs" title="Catacombs">Catacombs</a>. Rome is the third most visited city in the EU, after London and Paris, and receives an average of 7–10 million tourists a year, which sometimes doubles on holy years. The Colosseum (4 million tourists) and the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Museums" title="Vatican Museums">Vatican Museums</a> (4.2 million tourists) are the 39th and 37th (respectively) most visited places in the world, according to a recent study.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-itvnews.tv_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-itvnews.tv-143">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rome is a major archaeological hub, and one of the world's main centres of <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">archaeological research</a>. There are numerous cultural and research institutes located in the city, such as the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_in_Rome" title="American Academy in Rome">American Academy in Rome</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[141]</a></sup> and The Swedish Institute at Rome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[142]</a></sup> Rome contains numerous <a href="/wiki/List_of_ancient_monuments_in_Rome" title="List of ancient monuments in Rome">ancient sites</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Forum" title="Roman Forum">Forum Romanum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trajan%27s_Market" title="Trajan's Market">Trajan's Market</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trajan%27s_Forum" title="Trajan's Forum">Trajan's Forum</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[143]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Colosseum" title="Colosseum">Colosseum</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pantheon,_Rome" title="Pantheon, Rome">Pantheon</a>, to name but a few. The <a href="/wiki/Colosseum" title="Colosseum">Colosseum</a>, arguably one of Rome's most iconic archaeological sites, is regarded as a <a href="/wiki/Wonders_of_the_World" title="Wonders of the World">wonder of the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brewers_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-brewers-147">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miller_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-miller-148">[145]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rome contains a vast and impressive collection of art, sculpture, <a href="/wiki/Fountain" title="Fountain">fountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mosaic" title="Mosaic">mosaics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fresco" title="Fresco">frescos</a>, and paintings, from all different periods. Rome first became a major artistic centre during ancient Rome, with forms of important <a href="/wiki/Roman_art" title="Roman art">Roman art</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Architecture_of_ancient_Rome" title="Architecture of ancient Rome">architecture</a>, painting, sculpture and <a href="/wiki/Mosaic" title="Mosaic">mosaic</a> work. <a href="/wiki/Metalworking" title="Metalworking">Metal-work</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coin_die" title="Coin die">coin die</a> and gem engraving, <a href="/wiki/Ivory_carving" title="Ivory carving">ivory carvings</a>, figurine glass, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Roman_pottery" title="Ancient Roman pottery">pottery</a>, and book illustrations are considered to be 'minor' forms of Roman artwork.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[146]</a></sup> Rome later became a major centre of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> art, since the popes spent vast sums of money for the constructions of grandiose <a href="/wiki/Basilica" title="Basilica">basilicas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palace" title="Palace">palaces</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piazza" title="Piazza">piazzas</a> and public buildings in general. Rome became one of Europe's major centres of Renaissance artwork, second only to <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, and able to compare to other major cities and cultural centres, such as Paris and <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>. The city was affected greatly by the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Baroque" title="Italian Baroque">baroque</a>, and Rome became the home of numerous artists and architects, such as <a href="/wiki/Gian_Lorenzo_Bernini" title="Gian Lorenzo Bernini">Bernini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caravaggio" title="Caravaggio">Caravaggio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annibale_Carracci" title="Annibale Carracci">Carracci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Borromini" title="Francesco Borromini">Borromini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pietro_da_Cortona" title="Pietro da Cortona">Cortona</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[147]</a></sup> In the late 18th century and early 19th century, the city was one of the centres of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Tour" title="Grand Tour">Grand Tour</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[148]</a></sup> when wealthy, young English and other European aristocrats visited the city to learn about <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_ancient_Rome" title="Culture of ancient Rome">ancient Roman culture</a>, art, philosophy, and architecture. Rome hosted a great number of neoclassical and rococo artists, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giovanni_Paolo_Pannini" title="Giovanni Paolo Pannini">Pannini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Bellotto" title="Bernardo Bellotto">Bernardo Bellotto</a>. Today, the city is a major artistic centre, with numerous art institutes<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[149]</a></sup> and museums.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:608px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colosseo_di_Roma_panoramic.jpg" title="Internal view of the Colosseum"><img alt="" data-file-height="3854" data-file-width="7335" decoding="async" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Colosseo_di_Roma_panoramic.jpg/600px-Colosseo_di_Roma_panoramic.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Colosseo_di_Roma_panoramic.jpg/900px-Colosseo_di_Roma_panoramic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Colosseo_di_Roma_panoramic.jpg/1200px-Colosseo_di_Roma_panoramic.jpg 2x" width="600"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Colosseo_di_Roma_panoramic.jpg" title="File:Colosseo di Roma panoramic.jpg"> </a></div>Internal view of the Colosseum</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vatican_Museums_Spiral_Staircase_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2756" data-file-width="4336" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Vatican_Museums_Spiral_Staircase_2012.jpg/220px-Vatican_Museums_Spiral_Staircase_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Vatican_Museums_Spiral_Staircase_2012.jpg/330px-Vatican_Museums_Spiral_Staircase_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Vatican_Museums_Spiral_Staircase_2012.jpg/440px-Vatican_Museums_Spiral_Staircase_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vatican_Museums_Spiral_Staircase_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Museums" title="Vatican Museums">Vatican Museums</a> are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_most_visited_art_museums" title="List of most visited art museums">3rd</a> most visited art museum in the world.</div></div></div>
<p>Rome has a growing stock of contemporary and modern art and architecture. The National Gallery of Modern Art has works by Balla, Morandi, Pirandello, Carrà, De Chirico, De Pisis, Guttuso, Fontana, Burri, Mastroianni, Turcato, Kandisky, and Cézanne on permanent exhibition. 2010 saw the opening of Rome's newest arts foundation, a contemporary art and architecture gallery designed by acclaimed Iraqi architect Zaha Hadid. Known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MAXXI_%E2%80%93_National_Museum_of_the_21st_Century_Arts" title="MAXXI – National Museum of the 21st Century Arts">MAXXI – National Museum of the 21st Century Arts</a> it restores a dilapidated area with striking modern architecture. Maxxi<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[150]</a></sup> features a campus dedicated to culture, experimental research laboratories, international exchange and study and research. It is one of Rome's most ambitious modern architecture projects alongside <a href="/wiki/Renzo_Piano" title="Renzo Piano">Renzo Piano</a>'s Auditorium Parco della Musica<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[151]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Massimiliano_Fuksas" title="Massimiliano Fuksas">Massimiliano Fuksas</a>' Rome Convention Center, Centro Congressi Italia EUR, in the EUR district, due to open in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[152]</a></sup> The convention centre features a huge translucent container inside which is suspended a steel and teflon structure resembling a cloud and which contains meeting rooms and an auditorium with two piazzas open to the neighbourhood on either side.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fontana.della.barcaccia.arp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1687" data-file-width="2130" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Fontana.della.barcaccia.arp.jpg/220px-Fontana.della.barcaccia.arp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Fontana.della.barcaccia.arp.jpg/330px-Fontana.della.barcaccia.arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Fontana.della.barcaccia.arp.jpg/440px-Fontana.della.barcaccia.arp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fontana.della.barcaccia.arp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Via_Condotti" title="Via Condotti">Via Condotti</a></div></div></div>
<p>Rome is also widely recognised as a world <a href="/wiki/Fashion_capital" title="Fashion capital">fashion capital</a>. Although not as important as Milan, Rome is the fourth most important centre for fashion in the world, according to the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Global_Language_Monitor" title="Global Language Monitor">Global Language Monitor</a> after <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, and beating <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[153]</a></sup>
</p><p>Major luxury fashion houses and jewellery chains, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valentino_SpA" title="Valentino SpA">Valentino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgari" title="Bulgari">Bulgari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fendi" title="Fendi">Fendi</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[154]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Laura_Biagiotti" title="Laura Biagiotti">Laura Biagiotti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brioni_(brand)" title="Brioni (brand)">Brioni</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Renato_Balestra" title="Renato Balestra">Renato Balestra</a>, are headquartered or were founded in the city. Also, other major labels, such as <a href="/wiki/Gucci" title="Gucci">Gucci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chanel" title="Chanel">Chanel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prada" title="Prada">Prada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolce_%26_Gabbana" title="Dolce &amp; Gabbana">Dolce &amp; Gabbana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armani" title="Armani">Armani</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Versace" title="Versace">Versace</a> have luxury boutiques in Rome, primarily along its prestigious and upscale <a href="/wiki/Via_Condotti" title="Via Condotti">Via dei Condotti</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Roman_cuisine" title="Roman cuisine">Roman cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spaghetti_alla_Carbonara.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Spaghetti_alla_Carbonara.jpg/220px-Spaghetti_alla_Carbonara.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Spaghetti_alla_Carbonara.jpg/330px-Spaghetti_alla_Carbonara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Spaghetti_alla_Carbonara.jpg/440px-Spaghetti_alla_Carbonara.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spaghetti_alla_Carbonara.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Spaghetti <a href="/wiki/Carbonara" title="Carbonara">alla carbonara</a></i>, a typical Roman dish</div></div></div>
<p>Rome's cuisine has evolved through centuries and periods of social, cultural, and political changes. Rome became a major gastronomical centre during the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">ancient age</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Roman_cuisine" title="Ancient Roman cuisine">Ancient Roman cuisine</a> was highly influenced by Ancient Greek culture, and after, the empire's enormous expansion exposed Romans to many new, provincial culinary habits and cooking techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rome's cuisine has evolved through centuries and periods of social, cultural, and political changes. Rome became a major gastronomical centre during the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">ancient age</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Roman_cuisine" title="Ancient Roman cuisine">Ancient Roman cuisine</a> was highly influenced by Ancient Greek culture, and after, the empire's enormous expansion exposed Romans to many new, provincial culinary habits and cooking techniques.
</p><p>Later, during the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, Rome became well known as a centre of high-cuisine, since some of the best chefs of the time worked for the popes. An example of this was <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeo_Scappi" title="Bartolomeo Scappi">Bartolomeo Scappi</a>, who was a chef working for <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IV" title="Pope Pius IV">Pius IV</a> in the Vatican kitchen, and he acquired fame in 1570 when his cookbook <i>Opera dell'arte del cucinare</i> was published. In the book he lists approximately 1000 recipes of the Renaissance <a href="/wiki/Cuisine" title="Cuisine">cuisine</a> and describes cooking techniques and tools, giving the first known picture of a <a href="/wiki/Fork" title="Fork">fork</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[156]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Concia_di_zucchine.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2340" data-file-width="4160" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Concia_di_zucchine.jpg/220px-Concia_di_zucchine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Concia_di_zucchine.jpg/330px-Concia_di_zucchine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Concia_di_zucchine.jpg/440px-Concia_di_zucchine.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Concia_di_zucchine.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Concia di zucchine</i>, an example of Roman-Jewish cuisine</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Testaccio" title="Testaccio">Testaccio</a>, Rome's trade and slaughterhouse area, was often known as the "belly" or "slaughterhouse" of Rome, and was inhabited by butchers, or <i>vaccinari</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eyewitness_Travel_2006_pg._312_-_313_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eyewitness_Travel_2006_pg._312_-_313-160">[157]</a></sup> The most common or ancient Roman cuisine included the "fifth quarter".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eyewitness_Travel_2006_pg._312_-_313_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-Eyewitness_Travel_2006_pg._312_-_313-160">[157]</a></sup> The old-fashioned <i><a href="/wiki/Coda_alla_vaccinara" title="Coda alla vaccinara">coda alla vaccinara</a></i> (oxtail cooked in the way of butchers)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eyewitness_Travel_2006_pg._312_-_313_160-2"><a href="#cite_note-Eyewitness_Travel_2006_pg._312_-_313-160">[157]</a></sup> is still one of the city's most popular meals and is part of most of Rome's restaurants' menus. Lamb is also a very popular part of Roman cuisine, and is often roasted with spices and herbs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eyewitness_Travel_2006_pg._312_-_313_160-3"><a href="#cite_note-Eyewitness_Travel_2006_pg._312_-_313-160">[157]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the modern age, the city developed its own peculiar cuisine, based on products of the nearby <a href="/wiki/Roman_Campagna" title="Roman Campagna">Campagna</a>, as lamb and vegetables (<a href="/wiki/Artichoke" title="Artichoke">globe artichokes</a> are common).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[158]</a></sup> In parallel, Roman Jews – present in the city since the 1st century BC – developed their own cuisine, the <i>cucina giudaico-romanesca</i>.
</p><p>Examples of Roman dishes include <i><a href="/wiki/Saltimbocca" title="Saltimbocca">saltimbocca</a> alla romana</i> – a veal cutlet, Roman-style, topped with raw ham and sage and simmered with white wine and butter; <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carciofi_alla_romana" title="Carciofi alla romana">carciofi alla romana</a></i> – artichokes Roman-style, outer leaves removed, stuffed with mint, garlic, breadcrumbs and braised; <i><a href="/wiki/Carciofi_alla_giudia" title="Carciofi alla giudia">carciofi alla giudia</a></i> – artichokes fried in olive oil, typical of Roman Jewish cooking, outer leaves removed, stuffed with mint, garlic, breadcrumbs and braised; <i><a href="/wiki/Carbonara" title="Carbonara">spaghetti alla carbonara</a></i> – <a href="/wiki/Spaghetti" title="Spaghetti">spaghetti</a> with <a href="/wiki/Bacon" title="Bacon">bacon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egg_(food)" title="Egg (food)">eggs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pecorino" title="Pecorino">pecorino</a>; and <i><a href="/wiki/Gnocchi_alla_romana" title="Gnocchi alla romana">gnocchi di semolino alla romana</a></i> – <a href="/wiki/Semolina" title="Semolina">semolina</a> dumpling, Roman-style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[159]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span></h3>
<p>In 2021, Rome was "invaded" by feral boars which plundered trash, disrupted traffic, and threatened residents. There are now approximately 5,000–6,000 wild boars in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[160]</a></sup> Mayor <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Raggi" title="Virginia Raggi">Virginia Raggi</a> sued the <a href="/wiki/Lazio" title="Lazio">Lazio</a> region for failing to defend the city, while other critics have faulted Rome's failure at trash collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[161]</a></sup> “We must act as soon as possible and involve the army if necessary,” said Coldiretti, a farmers association.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[162]</a></sup>
</p><p>Picnics were banned in northern Rome as health authorities move to contain the <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boar</a> population after <a href="/wiki/African_swine_fever_virus" title="African swine fever virus">African swine fever</a> was detected in a deceased animal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[163]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_set_in_Rome" title="List of films set in Rome">List of films set in Rome</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_set_in_ancient_Rome" title="List of films set in ancient Rome">List of films set in ancient Rome</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:198px;max-width:198px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:141px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Cinecitt%C3%A0_-_Entrance.jpg/392px-Cinecitt%C3%A0_-_Entrance.jpg 2x" width="196"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Cinecitt%C3%A0" title="Cinecittà">Cinecittà studios</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:190px;max-width:190px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:141px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audrey_Hepburn_and_Gregory_Peck_on_Vespa_in_Roman_Holiday_trailer.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1440" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Audrey_Hepburn_and_Gregory_Peck_on_Vespa_in_Roman_Holiday_trailer.jpg/188px-Audrey_Hepburn_and_Gregory_Peck_on_Vespa_in_Roman_Holiday_trailer.jpg"
