1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Audrey_Hepburn_and_Gregory_Peck_on_Vespa_in_Roman_Holiday_trailer.jpg/376px-Audrey_Hepburn_and_Gregory_Peck_on_Vespa_in_Roman_Holiday_trailer.jpg 2x" width="188"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Holiday_(1953_film)" title="Roman Holiday (1953 film)">Roman Holiday</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Audrey_Hepburn" title="Audrey Hepburn">Audrey Hepburn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Peck" title="Gregory Peck">Gregory Peck</a>, 1953</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Rome hosts the <a href="/wiki/Cinecitt%C3%A0" title="Cinecittà">Cinecittà Studios</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-romefile1_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-romefile1-167">[164]</a></sup> the largest film and television production facility in continental Europe and the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Italy" title="Cinema of Italy">Italian cinema</a>, where many of today's biggest box office hits are filmed. The 99-acre (40 ha) studio complex is 9.0 km (5.6 mi) from the centre of Rome and is part of one of the biggest production communities in the world, second only to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Hollywood, Los Angeles, California">Hollywood</a>, with well over 5,000 professionals – from period costume makers to visual effects specialists. More than 3,000 productions have been made on its lot, from recent features like <i><a href="/wiki/The_Passion_of_the_Christ" title="The Passion of the Christ">The Passion of the Christ</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gangs_of_New_York" title="Gangs of New York">Gangs of New York</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Rome_(TV_series)" title="Rome (TV series)">HBO's <i>Rome</i></a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Life_Aquatic_with_Steve_Zissou" title="The Life Aquatic with Steve Zissou">The Life Aquatic</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Dino_De_Laurentiis" title="Dino De Laurentiis">Dino De Laurentiis</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/The_Decameron" title="The Decameron">Decameron</a></i>, to such cinema classics as <i><a href="/wiki/Ben-Hur_(1959_film)" title="Ben-Hur (1959 film)">Ben-Hur</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Cleopatra_(1963_film)" title="Cleopatra (1963 film)">Cleopatra</a></i>, and the films of <a href="/wiki/Federico_Fellini" title="Federico Fellini">Federico Fellini</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Founded in 1937 by <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>, the studios were bombed by the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Western Allies</a> during the Second World War. In the 1950s, Cinecittà was the filming location for several large American film productions, and subsequently became the studio most closely associated with <a href="/wiki/Federico_Fellini" title="Federico Fellini">Federico Fellini</a>. Today, Cinecittà is the only studio in the world with pre-production, production, and full post-production facilities on one lot, allowing directors and producers to walk in with their script and "walkout" with a completed film.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_dialect" title="Roman dialect">Roman dialect</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DM_TI_Claudius_Tiberinus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1089" data-file-width="1983" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/DM_TI_Claudius_Tiberinus.jpg/290px-DM_TI_Claudius_Tiberinus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/DM_TI_Claudius_Tiberinus.jpg/435px-DM_TI_Claudius_Tiberinus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/DM_TI_Claudius_Tiberinus.jpg/580px-DM_TI_Claudius_Tiberinus.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DM_TI_Claudius_Tiberinus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sepulchral inscription for Tiberius Claudius Tiberinus, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plebeian" title="Plebeian">Plebeian</a> and professional declaimer of poetry. 1st century AD, <a href="/wiki/Museo_Nazionale_Romano" title="Museo Nazionale Romano">Museo Nazionale Romano</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[165]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Although associated today only with Latin, ancient Rome was in fact multilingual. In the highest antiquity, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sabine" title="Sabine">Sabine</a> tribes shared the area of what is today Rome with Latin tribes. The Sabine language was one of the <a href="/wiki/Italic_languages" title="Italic languages">Italic</a> group of ancient Italian languages, along with Etruscan, which would have been the main language of the last three kings who ruled the city till the founding of the Republic in 509 BC. Urganilla, or <a href="/wiki/Plautia_Urgulanilla" title="Plautia Urgulanilla">Plautia Urgulanilla</a>, wife of Emperor Claudius, is thought to have been a speaker of Etruscan many centuries after this date, according to Suetonius' entry on Claudius. However Latin, in various evolving forms, was the main language of classical Rome, but as the city had immigrants, slaves, residents, ambassadors from many parts of the world it was also multilingual. Many educated Romans also spoke Greek, and there was a large Greek, Syriac and Jewish population in parts of Rome from well before the Empire.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> evolved during the Middle Ages into a new language, the "<i>volgare</i>". The latter emerged as the confluence of various regional dialects, among which the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuscan_language" title="Tuscan language">Tuscan dialect</a> predominated, but the population of Rome also developed its own dialect, the <a href="/wiki/Romanesco_dialect" title="Romanesco dialect">Romanesco</a>. The <i>Romanesco</i> spoken during the Middle Ages was more like a southern Italian dialect, very close to the <a href="/wiki/Neapolitan_language" title="Neapolitan language">Neapolitan language</a> in <a href="/wiki/Campania" title="Campania">Campania</a>. The influence of the <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florentine</a> culture during the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">renaissance</a>, and above all, the immigration to Rome of many Florentines following the two <a href="/wiki/House_of_Medici" title="House of Medici">Medici</a> Popes (<a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_X" title="Pope Leo X">Leo X</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_VII" title="Pope Clement VII">Clement VII</a>), caused a major shift in the dialect, which began to resemble more the Tuscan varieties. This remained largely confined to Rome until the 19th century, but then expanded to other zones of <a href="/wiki/Lazio" title="Lazio">Lazio</a> (<a href="/wiki/Civitavecchia" title="Civitavecchia">Civitavecchia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latina,_Lazio" title="Latina, Lazio">Latina</a> and others), from the beginning of the 20th century, thanks to the rising population of Rome and to improving transportation systems. As a consequence of education and media like radio and television, Romanesco became more similar to standard Italian but does not represent standard Italian. Dialectal literature in the traditional form of Romanesco includes the works of such authors as <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Gioachino_Belli" title="Giuseppe Gioachino Belli">Giuseppe Gioachino Belli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trilussa" title="Trilussa">Trilussa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cesare_Pascarella" title="Cesare Pascarella">Cesare Pascarella</a>. It is worth remembering though that Romanesco was a "<i>lingua vernacola</i>" (vernacular language), meaning that for centuries, it did not have a written form but it was only spoken by the population.
</p><p>Contemporary Romanesco is mainly represented by popular actors and actresses, such as <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Sordi" title="Alberto Sordi">Alberto Sordi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aldo_Fabrizi" title="Aldo Fabrizi">Aldo Fabrizi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anna_Magnani" title="Anna Magnani">Anna Magnani</a>. <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Verdone" title="Carlo Verdone">Carlo Verdone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Montesano" title="Enrico Montesano">Enrico Montesano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gigi_Proietti" title="Gigi Proietti">Gigi Proietti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nino_Manfredi" title="Nino Manfredi">Nino Manfredi</a>.
</p><p>Rome's historic contribution to language in a worldwide sense is much more extensive, however. Through the process of <a href="/wiki/Romanization_(cultural)" title="Romanization (cultural)">Romanization</a>, the peoples of Italy, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallia" title="Gallia">Gallia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dacia" title="Dacia">Dacia</a> developed languages which derive directly from Latin and were adopted in large areas of the world, all through cultural influence, colonisation and migration. Moreover, also modern English, because of the <a href="/wiki/Norman_Conquest" title="Norman Conquest">Norman Conquest</a>, borrowed a large percentage of its vocabulary from the Latin language. The <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Roman or Latin alphabet</a> is the most widely used writing system in the world used by the greatest number of languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[166]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rome has long hosted artistic communities, foreign resident communities and many foreign religious students or <a href="/wiki/Christian_pilgrimage" title="Christian pilgrimage">pilgrims</a> and so has always been a multilingual city. Today because of mass tourism, many languages are used in servicing tourism, especially English which is widely known in tourist areas, and the city hosts large numbers of immigrants and so has many multilingual immigrant areas.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:L%27Olimpico_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/L%27Olimpico_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-L%27Olimpico_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/L%27Olimpico_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-L%27Olimpico_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/L%27Olimpico_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-L%27Olimpico_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:L%27Olimpico_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stadio_Olimpico" title="Stadio Olimpico">Stadio Olimpico</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">A.S. Roma</a> and <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">S.S. Lazio</a>, is one of the largest in Europe, with a capacity of over 70,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[167]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is the most popular sport in Rome, as in the rest of the country.
The city hosted the final games of the <a href="/wiki/1934_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1934 FIFA World Cup">1934</a> and <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 FIFA World Cup</a>.
The latter took place in the <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Olimpico" title="Stadio Olimpico">Stadio Olimpico</a>, which is also the shared home stadium for local <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> clubs <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">S.S. Lazio</a>, founded in 1900, and <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">A.S. Roma</a>, founded in 1927, whose rivalry in the <a href="/wiki/Derby_della_Capitale" title="Derby della Capitale">Derby della Capitale</a> has become a staple of Roman sports culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[168]</a></sup>
Footballers who play for these teams and are also born in the city tend to become especially popular, as has been the case with players such as <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Totti" title="Francesco Totti">Francesco Totti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniele_De_Rossi" title="Daniele De Rossi">Daniele De Rossi</a> (both for A.S. Roma), and <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Nesta" title="Alessandro Nesta">Alessandro Nesta</a> (for S.S. Lazio).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roma_-_Stadio_Olimpico_-_Stadio_dei_Marmi_-_Andrea_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="672" data-file-width="896" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Roma_-_Stadio_Olimpico_-_Stadio_dei_Marmi_-_Andrea_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Roma_-_Stadio_Olimpico_-_Stadio_dei_Marmi_-_Andrea_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Roma_-_Stadio_Olimpico_-_Stadio_dei_Marmi_-_Andrea_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Roma_-_Stadio_Olimpico_-_Stadio_dei_Marmi_-_Andrea_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Roma_-_Stadio_Olimpico_-_Stadio_dei_Marmi_-_Andrea_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Roma_-_Stadio_Olimpico_-_Stadio_dei_Marmi_-_Andrea_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roma_-_Stadio_Olimpico_-_Stadio_dei_Marmi_-_Andrea_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stadio_dei_Marmi" title="Stadio dei Marmi">Stadio dei Marmi</a></div></div></div>
<p>Rome hosted the <a href="/wiki/1960_Summer_Olympics" title="1960 Summer Olympics">1960 Summer Olympics</a>, with great success, using many ancient sites such as the <a href="/wiki/Villa_Borghese" title="Villa Borghese">Villa Borghese</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Baths_of_Caracalla" title="Baths of Caracalla">Thermae of Caracalla</a> as venues. For the Olympic Games many new facilities were built, notably the new large Olympic Stadium (which was then enlarged and renewed to host several matches and the final of the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 FIFA World Cup</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Flaminio" title="Stadio Flaminio">Stadio Flaminio</a>, the Villaggio Olimpico (Olympic Village, created to host the athletes and redeveloped after the games as a residential district), ecc. Rome made a <a href="/wiki/Rome_bid_for_the_2020_Summer_Olympics" title="Rome bid for the 2020 Summer Olympics">bid</a> to host the <a href="/wiki/2020_Summer_Olympics" title="2020 Summer Olympics">2020 Summer Olympics</a> but it was withdrawn before the deadline for applicant files.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-olympic.org_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-olympic.org-172">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bladesplace.id.au_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bladesplace.id.au-173">[170]</a></sup>
</p><p>Further, Rome hosted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1991_EuroBasket" title="1991 EuroBasket">1991 EuroBasket</a> and is home to the internationally recognised basketball team <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pallacanestro_Virtus_Roma" title="Pallacanestro Virtus Roma">Virtus Roma</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> is gaining wider acceptance.
Until 2011 the <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Flaminio" title="Stadio Flaminio">Stadio Flaminio</a> was the home stadium for the <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_rugby_union_team" title="Italy national rugby union team">Italy national rugby union team</a>, which has been playing in the <a href="/wiki/Six_Nations_Championship" title="Six Nations Championship">Six Nations Championship</a> since 2000. The team now plays home games at the Stadio Olimpico because the Stadio Flaminio needs works of renovation in order to improve both its capacity and safety.
Rome is home to local rugby union teams such as <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Roma_Olimpic" title="Rugby Roma Olimpic">Rugby Roma</a> (founded in 1930 and winner of five Italian championships, the latter in 1999–2000), <a href="/wiki/Unione_Rugby_Capitolina" title="Unione Rugby Capitolina">Unione Rugby Capitolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio_Rugby_1927" title="S.S. Lazio Rugby 1927">S.S. Lazio 1927</a> (rugby union branch of the multisport club S.S. Lazio).
</p><p>Every May, Rome hosts the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ATP_World_Tour_Masters_1000" title="ATP World Tour Masters 1000">ATP Masters Series</a> tennis tournament on the clay courts of the <a href="/wiki/Foro_Italico" title="Foro Italico">Foro Italico</a>. Cycling was popular in the post-World War II period, although its popularity has faded. Rome has hosted the final portion of the <a href="/wiki/Giro_d%27Italia" title="Giro d'Italia">Giro d'Italia</a> three times, in 1911, 1950, and 2009. Rome is also home to other sports teams, including volleyball (<a href="/wiki/M._Roma_Volley" title="M. Roma Volley">M. Roma Volley</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">handball</a> or <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">waterpolo</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Rome" title="Transport in Rome">Transport in Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rom_Fiumicino_2011-by-RaBoe-02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1300" data-file-width="2089" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Rom_Fiumicino_2011-by-RaBoe-02.jpg/220px-Rom_Fiumicino_2011-by-RaBoe-02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Rom_Fiumicino_2011-by-RaBoe-02.jpg/330px-Rom_Fiumicino_2011-by-RaBoe-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Rom_Fiumicino_2011-by-RaBoe-02.jpg/440px-Rom_Fiumicino_2011-by-RaBoe-02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rom_Fiumicino_2011-by-RaBoe-02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport" title="Leonardo da Vinci–Fiumicino Airport">Rome–Fiumicino Airport</a> was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">tenth busiest airport</a> in Europe in 2016.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Giorcescivitavecchia3.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Giorcescivitavecchia3.JPG/220px-Giorcescivitavecchia3.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Giorcescivitavecchia3.JPG/330px-Giorcescivitavecchia3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Giorcescivitavecchia3.JPG/440px-Giorcescivitavecchia3.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Giorcescivitavecchia3.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Civitavecchia" title="Port of Civitavecchia">Port of Civitavecchia</a></div></div></div>
<p>Rome is at the centre of the radial network of roads that roughly follow the lines of the ancient Roman roads which began at the <a href="/wiki/Capitoline_Hill" title="Capitoline Hill">Capitoline Hill</a> and connected Rome with its empire. Today Rome is circled, at a distance of about 10 km (6 mi) from the Capitol, by the ring-road (the <i><a href="/wiki/Grande_Raccordo_Anulare" title="Grande Raccordo Anulare">Grande Raccordo Anulare</a></i> or <i>GRA</i>).
</p><p>Due to its location in the centre of the Italian peninsula, Rome is the principal <a href="/wiki/Railway_node" title="Railway node">railway node</a> for central Italy. Rome's main railway station, <a href="/wiki/Roma_Termini_railway_station" title="Roma Termini railway station">Termini</a>, is one of the largest railway stations in Europe and the most heavily used in Italy, with around 400 thousand travellers passing through every day. The second-largest station in the city, <a href="/wiki/Roma_Tiburtina_railway_station" title="Roma Tiburtina railway station">Roma Tiburtina</a>, has been redeveloped as a <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Italy" title="High-speed rail in Italy">high-speed rail</a> terminus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[171]</a></sup> As well as frequent high-speed day trains to all major Italian cities, Rome is linked nightly by 'boat train' sleeper services to Sicily, and internationally by overnight sleeper services to Munich and Vienna by ÖBB Austrian railways.
</p><p>Rome is served by three airports. The intercontinental <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci-Fiumicino_Airport" title="Leonardo da Vinci-Fiumicino Airport">Leonardo da Vinci International Airport</a>, Italy's chief airport is located within the nearby <a href="/wiki/Fiumicino" title="Fiumicino">Fiumicino</a>, south-west of Rome. The older <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rome_Ciampino_Airport" title="Rome Ciampino Airport">Rome Ciampino Airport</a> is a joint civilian and military airport. It is commonly referred to as "Ciampino Airport", as it is located beside <a href="/wiki/Ciampino" title="Ciampino">Ciampino</a>, south-east of Rome. A third airport, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roma-Urbe" title="Roma-Urbe">Roma-Urbe</a> Airport, is a small, low-traffic airport located about 6 km (4 mi) north of the city centre, which handles most helicopter and private flights.
</p><p>Although the city has its own quarter on the Mediterranean Sea (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lido_di_Ostia" title="Lido di Ostia">Lido di Ostia</a>), this has only a marina and a small channel-harbour for fishing boats. The main harbour which serves Rome is <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Civitavecchia" title="Port of Civitavecchia">Port of Civitavecchia</a>, located about 62 km (39 mi) northwest of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>The city suffers from traffic problems largely due to this radial street pattern, making it difficult for Romans to move easily from the vicinity of one of the radial roads to another without going into the historic centre or using the ring-road. These problems are not helped by the limited size of Rome's metro system when compared to other cities of similar size. In addition, Rome has only 21 taxis for every 10,000 inhabitants, far below other major European cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[173]</a></sup> Chronic congestion caused by cars during the 1970s and 1980s led to restrictions being placed on vehicle access to the inner city-centre during the hours of daylight. Areas, where these restrictions apply, are known as Limited Traffic Zones (<i>Zona a Traffico Limitato</i> (ZTL) in Italian). More recently, heavy night-time traffic in <a href="/wiki/Trastevere" title="Trastevere">Trastevere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Testaccio" title="Testaccio">Testaccio</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quartiere_San_Lorenzo" title="Quartiere San Lorenzo">San Lorenzo</a> has led to the creation of night-time ZTLs in those districts.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roma_Metropolitana_e_Ferrovia_2012.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1498" data-file-width="1850" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Roma_Metropolitana_e_Ferrovia_2012.png/220px-Roma_Metropolitana_e_Ferrovia_2012.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Roma_Metropolitana_e_Ferrovia_2012.png/330px-Roma_Metropolitana_e_Ferrovia_2012.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Roma_Metropolitana_e_Ferrovia_2012.png/440px-Roma_Metropolitana_e_Ferrovia_2012.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roma_Metropolitana_e_Ferrovia_2012.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roma Metrorail and Underground map, 2016</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Inaugurazione_metro_B1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Inaugurazione_metro_B1.jpg/220px-Inaugurazione_metro_B1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Inaugurazione_metro_B1.jpg/330px-Inaugurazione_metro_B1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Inaugurazione_metro_B1.jpg/440px-Inaugurazione_metro_B1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Inaugurazione_metro_B1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Conca_d%27Oro_(Rome_Metro)" title="Conca d'Oro (Rome Metro)">Conca d'Oro</a> metro station</div></div></div>
<p>A 3-line metro system called the <i><a href="/wiki/Rome_Metro" title="Rome Metro">Metropolitana</a></i> operates in Rome. Construction on the first branch started in the 1930s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[174]</a></sup> The line had been planned to quickly connect the <a href="/wiki/Roma_Termini_railway_station" title="Roma Termini railway station">main railway station</a> with the newly planned E42 area in the southern suburbs, where 1942 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esposizione_universale_(1942)" title="Esposizione universale (1942)">World Fair</a> was supposed to be held. The event never took place because of war, but the area was later partly redesigned and renamed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esposizione_Universale_Roma" title="Esposizione Universale Roma">EUR</a> (Esposizione Universale di Roma: Rome Universal Exhibition) in the 1950s to serve as a modern business district. The line was finally opened in 1955, and it is now the south part of the B Line.
</p><p>The A line opened in 1980 from Ottaviano to Anagnina stations, later extended in stages (1999–2000) to Battistini. In the 1990s, an extension of the B line was opened from Termini to Rebibbia. This underground network is generally reliable (although it may become very congested at peak times and during events, especially the A line) as it is relatively short.
</p><p>The A and B lines intersect at Roma Termini station. A new branch of the B line (B1) opened on 13 June 2012 after an estimated building cost of €500 million. B1 connects to line B at Piazza Bologna and has four stations over a distance of 3.9 km (2 mi).
</p><p>A third line, the C line, is under construction with an estimated cost of €3 billion and will have 30 stations over a distance of 25.5 km (16 mi). It will partly replace the existing <a href="/wiki/Roma_Termini_railway_station" title="Roma Termini railway station">Termini</a>-Pantano rail line. It will feature full automated, driverless trains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[175]</a></sup> The first section with 15 stations connecting Pantano with the quarter of Centocelle in the eastern part of the city, opened on 9 November 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[176]</a></sup> The end of the work was scheduled in 2015, but archaeological findings often delay underground construction work.
</p><p>A fourth line, D line, is also planned. It will have 22 stations over a distance of 20 km (12 mi). The first section was projected to open in 2015 and the final sections before 2035, but due to the city's financial crisis, the project has been put on hold.
</p><p>Above-ground public transport in Rome is made up of a bus, tram and urban train network (FR lines). The bus, tram, metro and urban railways network is run by <i>Atac S.p.A.</i> (which originally stood for the Municipal Bus and Tramways Company, <i>Azienda Tramvie e Autobus del Comune</i> in Italian). The bus network has in excess of 350 bus lines and over eight thousand bus stops, whereas the more-limited tram system has 39 km (24 mi) of track and 192 stops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[177]</a></sup> There is also one <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybus</a> line, opened in 2005, and 
additional two lines were opened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juts2009_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-juts2009-181">[178]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="International_entities.2C_organisations_and_involvement"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="International_entities,_organisations_and_involvement">International entities, organisations and involvement</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FAO_sede.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1210" data-file-width="2025" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/FAO_sede.jpg/220px-FAO_sede.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/FAO_sede.jpg/330px-FAO_sede.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/FAO_sede.jpg/440px-FAO_sede.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FAO_sede.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">FAO</a> headquarters in Rome, Circo Massimo</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WFP_Headquarters_in_Rome.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1831" data-file-width="3476" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/WFP_Headquarters_in_Rome.jpg/220px-WFP_Headquarters_in_Rome.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/WFP_Headquarters_in_Rome.jpg/330px-WFP_Headquarters_in_Rome.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/WFP_Headquarters_in_Rome.jpg/440px-WFP_Headquarters_in_Rome.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WFP_Headquarters_in_Rome.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">WFP</a> headquarters in Rome</div></div></div>
<p>Among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_cities" title="Global cities">global cities</a>, Rome is unique in having two sovereign entities located entirely within its city limits, the Holy See, represented by the Vatican City State, and the territorially smaller <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Military_Order_of_Malta" title="Sovereign Military Order of Malta">Sovereign Military Order of Malta</a>. The Vatican is an enclave of the Italian <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital city</a> and a sovereign possession of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>, which is the Diocese of Rome and the supreme government of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>. For this reason, Rome has sometimes been described as the capital of two states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[180]</a></sup> Rome, therefore, hosts foreign embassies to the Italian government, to the Holy See, to the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Military_Order_of_Malta" title="Sovereign Military Order of Malta">Order of Malta</a> and to certain international organisations. Several international <a href="/wiki/Roman_Colleges" title="Roman Colleges">Roman Colleges</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontifical_Universities_in_Rome" title="Pontifical Universities in Rome">Pontifical Universities</a> are located in Rome.
</p><p>The Pope is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Rome" title="Bishop of Rome">Bishop of Rome</a> and its official seat is the <a href="/wiki/Archbasilica_of_Saint_John_Lateran" title="Archbasilica of Saint John Lateran">Archbasilica of Saint John Lateran</a> (of which the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_of_the_French_Republic" title="President of the French Republic">President of the French Republic</a> is <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ex_officio" title="Ex officio">ex officio</a></i> the "first and only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honorary_canons" title="Honorary canons">honorary canon</a>", a title held by the heads of the French state since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Henry_IV_of_France" title="King Henry IV of France">King Henry IV of France</a>). Another body, the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Military_Order_of_Malta" title="Sovereign Military Order of Malta">Sovereign Military Order of Malta</a> (SMOM), took refuge in Rome in 1834, due to the conquest of Malta by <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> in 1798. It is sometimes classified as having sovereignty but does not claim any territory in Rome or anywhere else, hence leading to dispute over its actual sovereign status.
</p><p>Rome is the seat of the so-called "Polo Romano"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[181]</a></sup> made up by three main international agencies of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> (FAO), the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> (WFP) and the <a href="/wiki/International_Fund_for_Agricultural_Development" title="International Fund for Agricultural Development">International Fund for Agricultural Development</a> (IFAD).
</p><p>Rome has traditionally been involved in the process of European political integration. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_EU" title="Treaties of the EU">Treaties of the EU</a> are located in <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_della_Farnesina" title="Palazzo della Farnesina">Palazzo della Farnesina</a>, the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Italy)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Italy)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>, because the Italian government is the depositary of the treaties. In 1957 the city hosted the signing of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Rome" title="Treaties of Rome">Treaty of Rome</a>, which established the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (predecessor to the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>), and also played host to the official signing of the proposed <a href="/wiki/Treaty_establishing_a_Constitution_for_Europe" title="Treaty establishing a Constitution for Europe">European Constitution</a> in July 2004.
</p><p>Rome is the seat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Olympic_Committee" title="European Olympic Committee">European Olympic Committee</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Defense_College" title="NATO Defense College">NATO Defense College</a>. The city is the place where the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">Statute of the International Criminal Court</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a> were formulated.
</p><p>The city hosts also other important international entities such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IDLO" title="IDLO">IDLO</a> (International Development Law Organisation), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICCROM" title="ICCROM">ICCROM</a> (International Centre for the Study of the Preservation and Restoration of Cultural Property) and the <a href="/wiki/UNIDROIT" title="UNIDROIT">UNIDROIT</a> (International Institute for the Unification of Private Law).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Italy" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Italy">List of twin towns and sister cities in Italy</a></div>
<p>Since 9 April 1956, Rome is exclusively and reciprocally <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> only with:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, France, 1956</li></ul>
<dl><dd><i>Solo Parigi è degna di Roma; solo Roma è degna di Parigi.</i> <span class="languageicon">(in Italian)</span></dd>
<dd><i>Seule Paris est digne de Rome; seule Rome est digne de Paris.</i> <span class="languageicon">(in French)</span></dd>
<dd>"Only Paris is worthy of Rome; only Rome is worthy of Paris."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paris1_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-Paris1-188">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paris2_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-Paris2-189">[186]</a></sup></dd></dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Also the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This hypothesis originates from the Roman Grammarian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maurus_Servius_Honoratus" title="Maurus Servius Honoratus">Maurus Servius Honoratus</a>. However, the Greek verb descends from the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_root" title="Proto-Indo-European root">Proto-Indo-European root</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/srew-" title="wikt:Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/srew-"><i>*srew-</i></a> (compare Ancient Greek ῥεῦμα (<i>rheûma</i>) 'a stream, flow, current', the Thracian river name Στρυμών (<i>Strumṓn</i>) and Proto-Germanic <i>*strauma-</i> 'stream'; if it was related, however, the Latin river name would be expected to begin with **<i>Frum-</i>, like Latin <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/frigeo" title="wikt:frigeo">frīgeō</a></i> 'to freeze' from the root <i>*sreyHg-</i>) and the Latin verb from <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/h%E2%82%83rew-" title="wikt:Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/h₃rew-"><i>*h₃rew-</i></a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This hypothesis originates from <a href="/wiki/Plutarch" title="Plutarch">Plutarch</a>.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-Faus-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Faus_64-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Faus, José Ignacio Gonzáles. "<i>Autoridade da Verdade – Momentos Obscuros do Magistério Eclesiástico</i>". Capítulo VIII: Os papas repartem terras – Pág.: 64–65 e Capítulo VI: O papa tem poder temporal absoluto – Pág.: 49–55. Edições Loyola. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/85-15-01750-4" title="Special:BookSources/85-15-01750-4">85-15-01750-4</a>. Embora Faus critique profundamente o poder temporal dos papas ("<i>Mais uma vez isso salienta um dos maiores inconvenientes do status político dos sucessores de Pedro</i>" – pág.: 64), ele também admite um papel secular positivo por parte dos papas ("<i>Não podemos negar que intervenções papais desse gênero evitaram mais de uma guerra na Europa</i>" – pág.: 65).</span>
</li>
